**BUILD loop-back #8 LANDED + DISCHARGE MET (2026-06-12):** the de-gate + FormGate-seam install is built, tested, and discharged on the production path. **Five commits** (suite 3023 → **3034 green**, lint clean throughout): `8541cd8` (refactor: `FormGate` → 3 args, BW-05) / `5eababe` (feat: install the destination-validity gate on the production path — BW-01..04 + V-01/V-02; `parse_check_form_gate` installed at the `v1_chat_completions` construction site via the `form_gate=` seam, FC-57 zero-Terminal-edits; recovery de-gated) / `b86f98f` (refactor: rename all `_spike_pi_*` → production names, BW-06..10) / `6d69ee5` (test: cover the de-gated recovery loop + real-gate→terminal degradation — the conformance scan's V-01/V-02 covered the bridge gate; the live recovery loop and the real-gate-through-Terminal path had no automated coverage, now closed). **One BUILD design decision (surfaced at the stewardship gate):** recovery is gated on **artifact-store presence** rather than the literal "unconditional" BW-03 — behaviorally identical in production (the factory always wires the store; the substrate path needs it to resolve content anyway), but keeps store-less unit drivers inert (the `_FakeToolDispatch` default deliverable is invalid Python, so a literal unconditional de-gate would have spuriously fired re-dispatch across the unit suite). The pre-mortem: "a driver built without a store" becomes the silent-no-recovery failure mode; protection (the bridge gate) is independent and unaffected; one production construction site, wires the store. **DISCHARGE RUN** (de-gated $0 real-OpenCode, working-tree serve :8765, qwen3:8b coder / qwen3:14b seat, opencode 1.15.5; `LLMORC_SPIKE_PI_GATE` no longer exists — gate runs by default): **criterion MET — 0 invalid files at the client across all 3 sessions.** Smoke: `cli.py` bled invalid form ×2 → server-side recovery re-dispatched and converged (`recovered=True redispatches=2`) → session converged 5/5, COMPLETE turn 6. Batch run 1: `converters.py` bled ×1 → recovered (`redispatches=1`) → converged. Batch run 2: stalled at turn 5 on **ollama marathon-degradation** (qwen3:14b seat-filler `httpx.ReadTimeout` + repeated `inference wait: elapsed=30` after ~95 min continuous load — the σ failure mode; orthogonal to ADR-041), floored per the runbook step-6 / σ precedent; even degraded its 4 produced files were all valid (0 invalid). **The gate+recovery fired and converged in BOTH completed sessions — the cheap coder genuinely bled and the de-gated production recovery caught it; this is not "0 invalid by luck."** The full reliability stack fired together live (REMAINING/COMPLETE termination judgment, ADR-039 content anchor `anchor=true`, completeness gate, capability-matched routing README→prose-improver, AND the new ADR-041 gate + recovery). **ADR-035 form-seam protection CA → install-discharged** (header + status updated; ADR-041 §Status updated). Evidence retained per spike-artifact retention: `scratch/spike-pi-form-adequacy-gate/{discharge_smoke,discharge}/` (SUMMARY.tsv, per-run validity + turns + serve-log slices) + `serve.log`. **STILL OPEN (practitioner to direct):** (step 4) coder-tier escalation — ADR-041 §Decision 5 convergence CA, the cheap→less-cheap→frontier ladder with the **frontier rung opt-in/cost-gated** + local-degradation path (ADR-014 lever; named-not-built; Arm E proved the lever in isolation n=6); (step 5) the deferred current-state doc sweep / BUILD Design Amendment (system-design / agents.md / ORIENTATION / field-guide for the loop-back-#8 mechanism — fold now or batch at cycle close per the WP-LB-A-onward deferral); the long-horizon axis-2 regime stays PLAY. ADR-041's convergence CA + long-horizon axis-2 remain open.

**BUILD loop-back #8 — coder-tier escalation ladder LANDED (step 4, 2026-06-12):** practitioner directed scope at the BUILD gate — **free 8b→14b rung built now (deterministic), frontier rung config-opt-in defaulting OFF, validate 14b efficacy as we go.** Grounding surfaced the ladder maps onto existing config: `code_generation` cheap=`agentic-tier-cheap-general` (qwen3:8b) / escalated=`agentic-tier-escalated-general` (qwen3:14b) are **both free** = ADR-041's cheap→less-cheap; the frontier (paid) rung was never wired = the opt-in addition. The validated-vs-free wrinkle: ADR-041's escalation evidence (Arm E) tested 8b-vs-MiniMax, NOT the free 14b rung — so the free rung's efficacy on persistent bleeds is the "validate as we go" item. **Four commits** (suite 3034 → **3044 green**, lint clean throughout): `ccef922` (feat: `OrchestratorToolDispatch.dispatch`/`_route`/`invoke_ensemble` honor a caller-forced `model_profile_override` taking precedence over the verdict-router selection, router still runs for observability; `ToolDispatcher` protocol extended, 7 test doubles updated for conformance; `_override_or_selected_profile` helper for complexity) / `541fa30` (refactor: extract `_form_invalid`/`_redispatch` recovery helpers + thread `model_profile_override` through `_delegate_generation`, inert; serving-surface double updated) / `7c48fc4` (feat: Loop Driver `escalation_ladder` — `_recover_invalid_form` walks the ordered ladder after the cheap cap, one re-dispatch per rung forcing the profile, stops at first valid, exhausted ladder → terminal refuses [local-degradation]; `TestLoopDriverFormEscalation` 4 tests) / `ac5658a` (feat: `OrchestratorConfig.form_escalation_frontier_profile` opt-in field + `_coder_escalation_ladder(config)` factory helper [free `escalated_tier` rung always + frontier when opted-in] wired into `get_loop_driver`; `TestCoderEscalationLadder` 3 + resolver 2 tests). **Determinism: trigger (parse-check failure → escalate) deterministic; ceiling (frontier) policy-gated — free rungs auto, paid frontier opt-in with local-degradation path = free-first preserved.** Mechanism unit+integration-validated; **session-level convergence-via-escalation is UNVALIDATED** (the discharge runs' bleeds were handled by cheap recovery, so escalation never fired live; the free-14b-vs-persistent-8b-bleed efficacy is the practitioner's "validate as we go" / PLAY item). **ADR-041's convergence CA remains open** (now wired, not yet session-validated); long-horizon axis-2 stays PLAY. Config opt-in surface: `orchestrator.form_escalation.frontier_profile: <paid-profile>` (omit for free-only ladder). **STILL OPEN:** step 5 doc sweep (fold #8 now or batch at cycle close); convergence-via-escalation live validation (PLAY/use); long-horizon axis-2 (PLAY).

**Escalation live-validation experiment (2026-06-12, $0 local) — premise FALSIFIED, useful finding.** Practitioner proposed deliberately undersizing the cheap coder ("a 2B that'd most certainly escalate from 2B to 8B") to force the escalation path to fire on-demand. Setup: temp profile `agentic-tier-tiny-coder` + `code_generation` tiers cheap=tiny/escalated=`agentic-tier-cheap-general` (8b); ladder = [8b]. **Four real-OpenCode sessions, escalation fired 0/4** — the undersized coder produced parse-VALID output every time: esc (qwen3.5:2b, converters+test) → both valid; esc2 (qwen3:0.6b, converters+test) → both valid; esc3 (0.6b, Calculator class w/ type hints+docstrings+ValueError) → valid 31-line class; esc4 (0.6b, **cli.py** argparse+main-guard, the documented σ/π bleed zone) → valid argparse. **Finding: the ADR-035 bare-output form directive is robust even at 0.6b** — undersizing the model does NOT reliably reproduce the form bleed; the σ/π bleeds were narrower/more stochastic (8b under specific conditions on the hardest file), not "any small model on a hard file." Implication: **the destination-validity gate is a rare-case backstop, not a frequently-needed crutch** (good news for production — the directive does most of the work), AND the live escalation path can't be demonstrated on-demand by model-undersizing. The escalation MECHANISM stays unit+integration-validated (the 4 `TestLoopDriverFormEscalation` tests + the real-gate→terminal integration test exercise the live code path with an in-process gate); **session-level convergence-via-escalation with a real model bleed remains for PLAY / real-deployment** when a genuine bleed occurs. Experiment config reverted (profile deleted, tiers restored to cheap=8b/escalated=14b — config clean vs HEAD); artifacts retained `scratch/escalation-validation/` (esc..esc4 SUMMARY.tsv + run slices + ws produced files).

**WP-LB-E LANDED — wrapper-contingency seam (the LAST loop-back WP, 2026-06-13):** commit `c09a886` (suite 3046 green, lint clean). The Loop Driver's per-turn generation boundary is now a construction-time-injectable strategy: a `GenerationTarget` protocol with `_CalleeGenerationTarget` (single-ensemble callee, FC-44) as the default; `_delegate_generation` routes its dispatch through it; the prep (form directive + content anchor + arg-parse), the control structure (`decide`), the Single-Step Enforcer, and the Terminal are unchanged. Default behavior byte-identical (callee is the default) — a structural affordance, not a behavior change (`refactor:`). FC-52 verified by `TestGenerationTargetSeam`: an injected wrapper-stub target produces the deliverable with the callee dispatch bypassed (the swap is injection-only). The wrapper impl (`DispatchPipeline.run` as the per-turn subroutine, ADR-033 §Rejected) stays a **recorded contingency, NOT built** — it depends on the single-turn pipeline (WP-B/C, pending). Fallback ordering documented on the protocol docstring (frontier-tier driver first per FC-46; wrapper reversion second-order, callee-incorrect FC-51 diagnosis only — split-incorrect → Design Amendment). **The tool-driven multi-turn surface is now functionally complete** — all WP-LB-* landed (A/B/C/D/E/G/H/I/J/K/L/M; F folded into J) + ADR-039/040/041 work. Remaining cycle items: the single-turn surface WP-B/C/D/E (separate, practitioner-decision); the field-guide / current-state doc sweep (cycle-close batch); a robust ladder/benchmark design (next); PLAY (axis-2 long-horizon + organic-bleed escalation).

**BENCHMARK LADDER DESIGN COMPLETE — feed-forward to a fresh-session build (2026-06-15):** practitioner directed a robust, repeatable ladder/benchmark to validate the reliability stack across task complexity + horizon and to generate the axis-2 evidence PLAY needs (replacing the ad-hoc discharge/escalation runner scripts). Designed via brainstorming + **research-methods-reviewed** (`housekeeping/audits/research-methods-benchmark-design.md` — 2 P1 + 5 P2 + 3 P3, all folded in). **Spec (approved, self-contained for a fresh session): `docs/agentic-serving/benchmark-design.md`.** Shape: one parameterized harness + a **horizon × complexity grid** read three ways — regression (per-cell pass/fail), axis-2 ceiling (highest passing cell), north-star tier comparison (cheap-local vs frontier, frontier opt-in/cost-gated). **Adaptive sampling** (n=1 coarse → mandatory n=3 ceiling-confirm → n=3–5 concentrate at computable boundary cells; pre-registered ≥2/3). **Hard-pass metrics:** form validity / convergence / content coherence / termination (deterministic, $0-checkable from produced files + serve-log slice). **Reported-not-gating:** delegation rate (per-cell denominator too small — ADR-036 threshold is a 24h window), escalation, churn. **Key review-driven design moves a fresh session MUST honor:** (1) form/escalation metrics are near-constant on the natural grid (the bare-output directive masks bleeds — the 0/4 undersize finding), so escalation is validated by a **dedicated adversarial bleed-injection probe**, NOT expected from the grid — this is also how the live convergence-via-escalation evidence (ADR-041 CA) finally gets produced; (2) the grid MUST include an expected-fail cell or the ceiling is only a lower bound; (3) harness robustness reqs are non-negotiable (unique `[BENCHMARK RUN {uuid4()}]` session marker; per-session log SLICE not cumulative; fresh-ollama + degradation smoke + tag-and-exclude; **separate `serve` instance** for dev-traffic isolation). **Code home: `benchmarks/agentic_serving/`** (corpus + runner + scorer + scorecard + CLI + README; separate from the pytest suite — never in CI; scorer/scorecard/boundary-fn/loader get unit tests, the runner is exercised live). **Prior harnesses to graduate from:** `scratch/spike-pi-form-adequacy-gate/` (validate.py + run_live_arm.sh) + `scratch/escalation-validation/` (the runner + the pitfalls they hit). **Deferred (out of scope):** published-benchmark translation (SWE-bench etc. — practitioner: maybe later/too difficult); edit/repair/bash task axis (greenfield-first); code semantic correctness (structural-reliability only — "parses-but-wrong" is PLAY). **NEXT (fresh session):** invoke `writing-plans` on the spec → step-by-step implementation plan → build `benchmarks/agentic_serving/` per the plan → run the first grid ($0 cheap-local) → scorecard. PLAY can consume the benchmark's axis-2 ceiling evidence.

The full grid is hours of local model time — run it deliberately. A 1-cell smoke validates the harness end-to-end first.

### FRESH-SESSION HANDOFF — launch the benchmark grid (the only remaining benchmark step)

The harness is built, reviewed, unit-tested (66), and live-de-risked. A fresh, lean session does the run (hours of local model time — kept out of the build thread per context discipline):

1. **Read:** `docs/agentic-serving/benchmark-design.md` (the build-and-run plan; §11 runbook) + `benchmarks/agentic_serving/README.md`. Do not re-derive — the design is research-methods-reviewed and the harness is committed.
2. **Pre-flight:** restart **ollama fresh** (the σ marathon-degradation guard); confirm `qwen3:8b` + `qwen3:14b` pulled; `opencode` 1.15.5 available.
3. **Run the grid ($0 cheap-local):** `uv run python -m benchmarks.agentic_serving.bench --config cheap-local` — manages its own serve on :8770, runs the pre-flight degradation smoke, then coarse (n=1) → ceiling-confirm (n=3) → concentrate (n=3 at boundary cells), writing a scorecard (md + JSON) under `benchmark-runs/`. Expect hours; if the smoke aborts (degraded), restart ollama and retry.
4. **Interpret the scorecard:** the ceiling frontier = the axis-2 evidence (ADR-033 §6b — the recorded load-bearing risk); per-cell pass/fail = the regression baseline; H4C4 is the P2-C expected-fail corner (if it passes, extend the grid upward).
5. **Then (optional, deliberate):** `--probe bleed-injection` produces the live convergence-via-escalation evidence (ADR-041 convergence CA — outstanding BUILD item #5); `--compare cheap-local,frontier --i-accept-frontier-cost` runs the north-star tier comparison (frontier is paid — opt-in; surface the estimate first). For the tier comparison the operator launches serve with the frontier-config profile, since the CLI records the named config as provenance and does not rewrite `config.yaml`.
6. **Feed PLAY:** the grid's axis-2 ceiling + the probe's escalation evidence are what PLAY consumes (it does not re-run ad hoc). BUILD stays OPEN until the 5 outstanding items are addressed (benchmark probe covers #5; #1 SAR store-hygiene is still the standalone code item).

**SPIKE τ COMPLETE — long-horizon on a 32GB machine answered + the anchor-overload fix landed (2026-06-16→17).** The benchmark grid (above) could not run on this 32GB rig as designed: the flat 300s per-cell timeout + the qwen3:8b/14b swap-thrash (the two models don't co-reside in 32GB) + marathon degradation timed cells out (the warm 2-file smoke alone took 445s, healthy). Practitioner reframe: the load-bearing question is *what config enables long-horizon agentic tasks on a 32GB commodity machine, mostly local with a few ¢ of frontier*. **Spike τ** answered it (pre-registered + methods-reviewed: `essays/research-logs/cycle-7-spike-tau-long-horizon-32gb.md`, `housekeeping/audits/research-methods-spike-tau.md`; ~5¢ total spend).

- **Answer (config now ADOPTED in `.llm-orc/config.yaml`):** **hosted qwen3.6-plus seat (Zen, paid) + local qwen3:8b coder + 8b→14b→MiniMax coder-tier escalation.** Seat question resolved: 8b too weak to orchestrate (arm S — sandbox-violating turn-1 write), local-14b too slow (arm A — ~250s/turn, the swap, not faster than ref), **hosted qwen both fast (~7s/turn seat) and capable** (arm B-qwen). MiniMax-as-SEAT fails (its strict chat template rejects the framework's tool-result message — B-mmx 400); MiniMax-as-CODER is fine (one-shot, the frontier escalation rung). Config carries a one-line `>>> SWAP TO FULLY-LOCAL / FREE` toggle. New profiles: `agentic-orchestrator-qwen36-zen`, `agentic-orchestrator-offline-8b`, `agentic-tier-frontier-coder-minimax`.
- **Ceiling + fix (ADR-042, landed):** with the adopted config the ladder converged clean through **10 files**, broke at ~12 — root cause **content-anchor overload** (ADR-039's all-prior-siblings anchor bloats/degrades the coder at scale; a form bleed across ALL coder tiers, escalation-proof since every tier gets the same bloated anchor). **Fix: bound the anchor (ADR-042 — `build_content_anchor(max_siblings=)`, `_CONTENT_ANCHOR_MAX_SIBLINGS=8`); landed + 3049-suite green, mypy/ruff clean.** Confirmed: l15 went 12/15 (broke) → 15/15 (clean) with the bound. **ADR-042 is Conditional Acceptance** — the spike's ladder template had an off-by-one bug (each step file instructed to import *itself*) confounding the exact threshold + coherence reads; discharge = a **clean coherence-at-scale re-run** (template already corrected in `scratch/spike-tau-long-horizon/run_arm.py`).
- **Corrected findings (recorded):** OpenCode has **no step cap** (`steps` is opt-in, unset) — the long-horizon limit was never client-side; it is framework-side (the now-bounded anchor). The benchmark's flat-300s-per-cell timeout is a latent harness gap (no horizon scaling). The CLI-test content-coherence wobble (test→cli `parse_args`) is stochastic (ADR-039-refinement territory). Earlier in-spike mis-attributions (routing-planner / client-cap / REMAINING-glitch) are all superseded in the research log by the raw-log ground truth.

### FRESH-SESSION HANDOFF (post-Spike-τ, 2026-06-17) — supersedes the benchmark-grid handoff above [SUPERSEDED: see the 2026-06-18 handoff below; ADR-042 reverted, J-3 fixed, anchor unbounded]

The benchmark-grid handoff above is **superseded**: the grid can't run on this 32GB rig as-designed, and Spike τ answered the question it was meant to (axis-2 long-horizon). To pick up:

1. **Read:** the Spike τ research log + ADR-042 + this entry. The config is adopted; the anchor fix is landed + suite-green; nothing is half-applied.
2. **Highest-value next step (ADR-042 discharge):** the clean coherence-at-scale re-run. The ladder template off-by-one is **fixed**; the adopted config bounds the anchor at K=8 by default (no env-gate). Run e.g. `LABEL=l20clean FILES=20 PYTHONPATH=. uv run python scratch/spike-tau-long-horizon/run_arm.py` (fresh ollama first) and check `coh=True` at scale → discharges ADR-042, confirms anchor-overload on a clean task, tunes K (or moves to dependency-scoped selection per Spike ξ).
3. **Then:** find the NEW ceiling above 15 (expected: accumulated conversation-context growth, NOT the anchor) — push l20/l30 clean.
4. **Config state:** ADOPTED (not reverted) per practitioner direction; paid qwen seat is the default (≈¢/session), local-swap is one toggle inline. The 3 new profiles + the spike env-gate removal are in place.
5. **Outstanding BUILD items unchanged** (§"OUTSTANDING BUILD ITEMS"): #1 SAR store-hygiene (standalone code), #5 ADR-041 convergence CA (the bleed-injection probe, now under the adopted config), etc. The benchmark harness stays built (for a faster rig later). Possible follow-up: a full argument-audit/methods-review on ADR-042 if a heavier DECIDE treatment is wanted (it was written as a focused amendment).

**J-3 over-extraction regression FOUND + FIXED (2026-06-18, debug mode-shift, $0 static).** The ADR-042 discharge runs (l10/l15 under the corrected call-form template) churned without terminating — l10: 50 REMAINING / 0 COMPLETE over 51 turns on a HEALTHY rig, all 10 files present and runnable (`main.py` → 512). Root cause confirmed statically (not the rig, not the coder): the J-3 requested-file regex `_REQUESTED_FILE_RE` matched the module-qualified call expressions the ADR-042 call-form template fix introduced (`step1.step1`, `base.start`) as **phantom deliverables**, so `requested − produced` never emptied and the deterministic gate stuck on REMAINING. **Distinct from the 2026-06-10-resolved Finding I** (empty-set/judge-fallback): the gate fires; `requested` was over-inflated, not empty. Decisive probe: `_extract_requested_deliverables(make_task(10))` returned 19 items (10 real + 9 phantom). Fix: restrict the regex extension to a recognized set (`_DELIVERABLE_EXTENSIONS`) + regression test + the `completeness:` diagnostic log restored as PERMANENT observability (its prior removal is why the churn was invisible/slow to diagnose); **suite 3050 green, lint clean, uncommitted**. **Constraint recorded in ADR-040 §Limitations** (the gate is coupled to task-prompt phrasing, so a task-wording change can silently break termination; the whitelist is a coverage boundary; structured deliverable-declaration is the deferred durable fix) — bounds future task/deliverable design. **ADR-042 (b) discharged** (run 3: the corrected-template chain executes, coherence is real, not a scorer false-pass); **(a) still NOT nailed** (the unbounded-clean l15 arm was masked by this same churn at 2 files; the isolated single-dispatch probe is the right instrument when desired). Spike τ runs retained per spike-artifact policy: `scratch/spike-tau-long-horizon/{l20clean,l20clean2,l10clean,l15unbound}-*`.

**ADR-042 (a)-isolation probe (Spike τ′, 2026-06-18, $0): the anchor-overload attribution REFUTED + the bound is net-negative.** Isolated single-dispatch probe (`scratch/spike-tau-anchor-overload/`, n=10/arm, qwen3:8b, the real `build_content_anchor` over run-1's 20 siblings, only the anchor varied) since the full-session ladder masked (a) under the J-3 churn. **Form-validity 10/10 in ALL three arms** — B_bounded(K=8, 440B) / A_unbounded(clean, 1.7KB) / A_fallback(full-content/bled, 6KB): the anchor does not overload the coder's form at any tested scale. **Reference resolution MONOTONIC in anchor content** (bounded 3/10 < unbounded 7/10 < fallback 10/10): the bound HURTS cross-file coherence, the opposite of its thesis. So ADR-042's overload mechanism is refuted and the K=8 bound is **net-negative** (no form benefit + a coherence cost); l15cap's empirical win is real but mis-attributed (candidate causes: stochastic / the now-fixed J-3 non-termination presenting as a stall / rig degradation — not the anchor). **Recorded in ADR-042 §Reassessment + the Spike τ research log §(a)-isolation probe.** The bound is **under reconsideration (revert / dependency-scoped selection / scale-gate) — practitioner-directed, pending.** ADR-042 (b) stays discharged (coherence real). Probe retained: `scratch/spike-tau-anchor-overload/`. (n=10 caveat: form 30/30 solid; resolution trend monotonic but individually borderline.)

### FRESH-SESSION HANDOFF (live benchmark run — the tier comparison + horizon re-confirm)

**Run plan (rig-managed — free-first; cheap arm ≈cents/session, Sonnet arm = in-session tokens; surface a cell count before the Sonnet dispatch):**

(the cycle's central claim); (b) the **post-J-3 horizon ceiling** — does the cheap arm now converge past ~12 files (l15/l20), or is the framework REMAINING→stop glitch still the wall? (ADR-033 §6b axis-2 CA). Both feed the PLAY discharge.

## Feed-Forward Signals

### From BUILD (loop-back #9 — skill/task/todowrite surface, for PLAY session design, 2026-06-18)

The collapse is done, but it sharpened an axis-2 / PLAY-design requirement that must be **explicit before the rig-gated PLAY run is designed** (ADR-033 §6c + §6b):

1. **The loop carries the full client tool surface, but its reliability machinery is file-action-shaped.** Grounded-carry (`CarryClientTool`) passes any client tool (`skill` / `task` / `todowrite`) through verbatim — a session using them won't crash. But the three reliability mechanisms are file-shaped: the **deterministic completeness gate** (ADR-040 — mines `name.ext` from task prose), the **content anchor** (ADR-039 — a cross-*file* baseline), and **delegated generation** (ADR-034 — maps to `write`/`edit` only). For skill/task/todowrite turns, termination falls to the **stochastic judge**, there is no content anchor, and generation cannot target a non-write tool.

2. **PLAY session design MUST exercise the richer surface, not just file-actions.** A file-actions-only PLAY session validates axis-2 long-horizon coherence on the *narrow* surface and silently misses the entire skill/task/todowrite gap. Design the run as a real RDD-style flow via OpenCode that deliberately triggers `todowrite` (multi-step planning state), `task` (sub-agent spawning), and `skill` (skill invocation) — the surface §6b names as "what a future run-RDD-via-OpenCode flow would use."

3. **Discovery targets to watch.** Where does the deterministic completeness gate fall to the stochastic judge (non-file deliverables)? Does a `task`-spawn turn terminate coherently, or does the loop mis-judge "done"? Does the absence of a content anchor cause cross-turn incoherence on non-file work? These are the requirements the real session surfaces — **the skill/task/todowrite work is discovered by PLAY, not built on spec; item 2 merges into the axis-2 run.**

4. **Rig is the design constraint, not a blocker (practitioner-clarified 2026-06-18).** The target rig is the 32GB box — permanently; no nicer hardware is being targeted. Design the PLAY run to work *here*: model sizing (local qwen3 seat + cheap coder), cool ollama between long runs, bound session length, and shape the validation to fit. The question is what makes axis-2 + skill/task/todowrite work on this box, not when better hardware arrives.

### From BUILD (§6 escalation probe, 2026-06-18)
1. **Form-recovery is robust enough to defeat adversarial bleed injection.** Across 3 live $0-local runs (1× 8b, 2× 0.6b) with a deliberately adversarial single-agent coder (always-fence + trailing-prose, fighting the bare-output directive), the deterministic gate caught every bleed (0 invalid files at the client) and the bounded cheap-tier recovery (cap 2, re-sample at default temperature) closed it every time — escalation never fired. The bleed is intermittent at every model size; one clean re-sample lands within the cap. Run B2 reached the last cheap retry (one re-sample short of cap exhaustion) but still recovered.
2. **The coder-tier escalation lever is a deeper backstop than the natural (or injected) failure distribution reaches.** It stays validated by the `TestLoopDriverFormEscalation` unit tests + the real-gate-through-terminal integration test (in-process gate injection drives the escalation code path directly) and Spike π Arm E (frontier closes a *forced* persistent bleed in isolation). Live escalate-and-converge is a PLAY / organic-deployment item — unmanufacturable by prompt/model injection because recovery is robust.
3. **The §6 probe is config-supplied, not harness-encoded.** `runner.py`/`bench.py` run probe cells identically to grid cells; the adversarial coder + tier ladder the §6 design names are operator config (the harness only marks `kind="probe"`). A future amendment could encode the adversarial coder, or — if live escalation evidence is ever wanted — inject it via a recovery-cap reduction rather than prompting. Recorded in `benchmark-design.md` §6.

### From BUILD (Spike τ/τ′ + J-3, 2026-06-18)
1. **The content anchor is exonerated and unbounded again.** The Spike τ′ isolation probe refuted ADR-042's anchor-overload mechanism (form 30/30 across unbounded / bounded / fallback) and showed the K=8 bound costs cross-file coherence (resolution 3 < 7 < 10). ADR-042 is reverted; ADR-039's all-prior selection stands. Do not re-introduce a bound without large-scale (>20-sibling) overload evidence; dependency-scoped selection is the indicated successor if it is ever needed.
2. **The deterministic completeness gate (ADR-040 / J-3) is coupled to task-prompt phrasing.** Its filename regex mines `name.ext` tokens from the task prose, so a task whose wording contains non-deliverable dotted tokens can break termination (the ADR-042 call-form fix did exactly this). The extension whitelist is the coverage boundary; structured deliverable-declaration is the durable fix. See ADR-040 §Limitations. Watch this when changing task templates or onboarding new deliverable types.
3. **The `completeness:` diagnostic log is now permanent.** Gate-fired-vs-judge-fallback plus the requested/produced/remaining counts are observable in serve.log; check it first when diagnosing any termination anomaly.
4. **ADR-041 convergence CA and axis-2 long-horizon remain the outstanding empirical gaps** (unchanged): the bleed-injection probe and PLAY/benchmark produce them. The named-file termination path is now validated, so multi-file convergence at scale is the next frontier, gated mostly by seat/coder capability and the rig, not by the framework.

### From BUILD (benchmark, 2026-06-15)
1. **The benchmark spec is the entry point** — `docs/agentic-serving/benchmark-design.md` is self-contained; read it + the research-methods audit before planning/building. Do not re-derive the design.
2. **Honor the research-methods fixes** — they are folded into the spec (adaptive ceiling-confirmation; form=regression-only + escalation-via-probe; expected-fail cell; pre-registered thresholds; separate-serve isolation). A build that drops them reintroduces the invalidating flaws the reviewer caught.
3. **The benchmark produces the axis-2 + escalation evidence the cycle's Conditional Acceptances need** — ADR-041 convergence CA (live escalate-and-converge, via the §6 probe) and ADR-033 §6b axis-2 long-horizon coherence (the ceiling frontier). PLAY consumes these, it does not re-run them ad hoc.
4. **Single-turn surface WP-B/C/D/E remains a separate practitioner decision** — not folded into "all items"; the tool-driven (north-star) surface is functionally complete.

**Origin:** Cycle 6 PLAY (2026-05-20) surfaced that the orchestrator-LLM's chain-handling behavior is the load-bearing failure for composition pipelines; ADR-022 amendment is empirically bounded to bare-endpoint mode and does not shift NL routing under tool-rich production clients. Spike δ confirmed that framework-driven Python chaining preserves data correctly across the same `web-searcher → claim-extractor` composition that failed under orchestrator-LLM routing. PLAY-tail grounding work (per susceptibility-snapshot recommendation) softened the initial "framework-driven pipeline" framing into bounded claims:

- Framework-driven **chain-handling** is well-grounded (Spike δ + alternatives belief-map confirm)
- Framework-driven **routing-decision** is contested — `tool_choice` constrained decoding is a viable lighter-weight alternative to a full routing-planner ensemble
- "Must-delegate to ensembles" is bounded to capability-matched requests, not universal
- The form-vs-content drift bifurcation may collapse if schema-as-enforcement unifies them

Cycle 6 status archived at `cycle-archive/cycle-6-ensemble-contract-observability-routing.md`.

**Cycle 7 question framing (provisional, for RESEARCH entry):**

Three linked architectural questions:

1. **Where does the routing decision live?** Options: (a) framework-driven routing-planner ensemble; (b) `tool_choice` constrained decoding forcing `invoke_ensemble` when a capability match is detected; (c) hybrid where a small classifier decides which mechanism applies per request. The chain-handling commitment is already framework-driven (Spike δ + belief-map); the routing-decision is the open territory.

2. **How are I/O contracts enforced?** Output_schema currently documentary (per Cycle 6 WP-D moderate advisory 1 resolution); claim-extractor's form drift demonstrates documentary schemas don't deliver compliance. Options: (a) schema-as-enforcement with reject-and-retry; (b) tool-call-as-output-format (agents call a `submit_results` tool whose params are the schema); (c) deterministic shaper after the agent (extra dispatch per ensemble with declared schema). Connects to form-vs-content drift collapse question — schema-as-enforcement might address both.

3. **What's the fallback shape for non-capability-matched requests?** Options: (a) general-completion fallback ensemble (preserves infrastructure, adds dispatch overhead); (b) direct LLM completion as residual through the orchestrator-LLM (preserves latency, loses infrastructure); (c) lightweight shim that wraps direct completion with minimal infrastructure (calibration verdict + audit log but no full ensemble overhead). The must-delegate-as-bounded framing means the fallback shape is design territory, not a forced choice.

These three questions are linked: the routing-decision mechanism + the contract-enforcement mechanism + the fallback shape together determine the cycle 7 architecture.

**Specific carry-forwards from Cycle 6 to address in Cycle 7 (or as standalone Thread A fixes between cycles):**

1. **`dispatch_log.json` overwrite vs. append.** Currently each chat-completions request overwrites the file with its own dispatches. Operator-facing post-hoc review use case is broken — the latest empty-dispatch request wipes prior session entries. Fix shape: append-mode, OR per-request files, OR reconstruct-from-artifacts at session close. Small fix; could land as Thread A (outside methodology cycle) or fold into Cycle 7 architecture work if the persistence semantics intersect the planner+synthesizer roles.

2. **`profile=?` placeholder in `dispatch start` log line.** Cosmetic — the profile is unknown at dispatch_start (resolved in `tier selection` one line later). Could be left blank, populated from the resolution step, or removed. One-line fix.

3. **Capability ensemble form drift at synthesizer/agent layer.** Claim-extractor's output is non-conformant to its `default_task` spec across all invocation paths. Cycle 7 DECIDE will land an ADR on I/O contract enforcement policy that addresses this directly.

**MODEL handling for Cycle 7:** Likely-needed. The architectural pivot introduces new vocabulary candidates: `routing-planner`, `response-synthesizer`, `general-completion fallback`, `plan-dispatch-synthesize pipeline`, `framework-as-orchestrator`. If RESEARCH + DISCOVER surface enough new vocabulary, formalize in `domain-model.md` before DECIDE. Decision deferred to DISCOVER's tail.

**DISCOVER handling for Cycle 7:** Required. The architectural pivot has stakeholder-mental-model implications:

- Tool User's "endpoint is a model" abstraction: holds or breaks under the new pipeline?
- Skill Orchestration User's "the orchestrator routes by capability under NL" mental model: now needs re-grounding given the routing-decision mechanism is design-open
- Ensemble Author / Operator: routing-planner authoring is a new authoring surface; what does the operator need to understand about the planner ensemble?
- Orchestrator LLM (as actor): its role shifts from decider to executor or disappears entirely — this is a stakeholder-model change worth surfacing

**ARCHITECT handling for Cycle 7:** Required. The chat-completions handler refactor is non-trivial: the orchestrator-LLM-as-decider goes away (or shrinks); new modules for routing-planner integration, synthesizer integration, plan-execution loop. Fitness criteria need to capture the new pipeline's invariants (e.g., "every chat-completions request resolves to ≥1 ensemble dispatch when a capability match exists"). Substantial ARCHITECT phase.

## BUILD-surfaced finding: termination suppression (Finding F) (2026-06-04)

**What surfaced.** The WP-LB-I acceptance run met the ADR-036 gating condition (delegation verified fired under natural phrasing) — and never finished. Every trailing turn was a no-new-task tool-result tail; the seat-filler delegated another revision of the same file each time (4 dispatches, 3 progressively rewritten `csv_helper.py` versions) until killed. The should-finish trailing shape was never in the 55/55 (ψ′ Arm C's trailing turns all carried a genuine new task).

**Characterization (Spike ψ″, pre-registered, 5 arms, $0 local).** E1 vs E2: with the C3 trailing guidance finish is 0/10; without it 10/10 — suppression is guidance-attributable. E3: a completion clause restores nothing (1/10) — position carries authority, wording does not remove it (the ψ.2-V2/ω.3b rhyme). E4a vs E4b (mid-task tail, work remaining): without guidance delegation is 0/10 (6/10 inline write — the Finding B north-star violation — and 4/10 premature finish); with guidance 9/10. **F-ψ″.3: the trailing guidance is simultaneously termination-suppressing on work-complete tails and delegation-carrying on work-remaining tails.** No composition of the current text resolves both; distinguishing the shapes requires a work-remaining signal the framework does not compute.

**Why it matters.** The north-star surface visibly fails on session convergence (headless runs never end; each zombie turn ≈ 4 min local compute), and Finding F inflates the delegation rate — ADR-036's ≥0.9 soak confirmation would be untrustworthy until termination is decided.

**Disposition (practitioner, 2026-06-04, after explained trade).** Loop-back #5: BUILD → DECIDE on the termination mechanism. Candidates: (a) conditional composition (needs a work-remaining signal); (b) framework-level termination policy (the thesis-consistent pole — belief-map it against alternatives rather than defaulting on pattern-rhyme, the loop-back #3 discipline); (c) restructured conditional guidance text (weakest; E3-wounded). WP-LB-J held pending the outcome — the mechanism plausibly extends the TurnDecision event shape J consumes.

## BUILD-surfaced finding: delegation reliability (Finding E) (2026-06-03)

**What surfaced.** The WP-LB-H acceptance runs showed the form contract works whenever delegation fires — and that delegation under a real client is ~coin-flip. Cumulative real-OpenCode evidence: 2 delegated / 2 grounded-carried under natural phrasing (WP-LB-G's run + today's three; the delegating OpenCode run used delegation-leaning phrasing). A direct-endpoint probe with the same tool shape but **without** OpenCode's system prompt delegated immediately — the suppressor is the client's system prompt out-competing `_DELEGATION_GUIDANCE` for the seat-filler's attention (the tension `loop_driver.py`'s guidance docstring recorded as "not a settled property").

**Why it matters.** The north-star value proposition (work delegated to ensembles) is structurally reachable but probabilistically gated on a cheap model's per-turn choice under an adversarial-prompt-budget contest the framework doesn't control. This is the exact contingency the WP-LB-C feed-forward pre-named as a DECIDE loop-back trigger ("on evidence, not speculation"). The evidence now exists, with a clean isolation.

**Disposition (practitioner, 2026-06-03).** Loop-back #3: BUILD → DECIDE on the delegation-decision mechanism, **grounded by Spike ψ first** — "this should be something we can vary and test." Spike ψ shape (DECIDE entry, $0 local): capture a real OpenCode request (client system prompt included) and replay variations against the endpoint, one lever at a time, n runs per variant, measuring delegation rate: (ψ.1) baseline under the current nudge; (ψ.2) guidance wording/position variants; (ψ.3) server-side `tool_choice` forcing on the seat-filler call (Ollama+qwen3 — Spike κ's negative was Zen/MiniMax, a different surface); (ψ.4) structural pre-filter split — the framework decides delegate-vs-carry, the seat-filler decides only the action shape (model-independent; consistent with the framework-guarantees-the-contract thesis: AS-9 / single-step enforcement / FC-53 directive-presence). DECIDE picks on measured rates. Candidate consideration: fold WP-LB-F's TurnDecision surfacing into the loop-back BUILD — it instruments exactly this measurement in production.

## BUILD-surfaced finding: deliverable-shape (Finding D) (2026-06-02)

**What surfaced.** The WP-LB-G real-OpenCode run delegated correctly (seat-filler → `invoke_ensemble` → `code-generator` → artifact → bridge → client `write`), but the `write` carried the raw ensemble result envelope (`{"results": {coder, critic, synthesizer}, "synthesis": null, …}`), not usable file content. Spike φ (`essays/research-logs/cycle-7-spike-phi-deliverable-shape.md`; $0 — code-reading + a no-model separability probe against the captured real artifact + 2 local claim-extractor runs) split Finding D into three separable layers:

- **D1 — extraction (BUILD).** `_extract_synthesizer_text` (`orchestrator_tool_dispatch.py:1373/1796`) succeeds only for a populated top-level `synthesis` (never set in the dependency-based model — `results_processor.py:21`) or a single-agent ensemble. Every multi-agent capability ensemble falls through to `json.dumps(raw_result)`. code-generator is the only multi-agent substrate-routed capability ensemble shipped → the only one bitten today, but the gap is structural. Internal where-sub-fork (executor-side populate vs envelope-side terminal-node pick) for the BUILD gate.
- **D2a — contract inert at execution (reopens a Cycle 6 call).** `default_task` has zero runtime reads (grep-proven; both the MCP-invoke and orchestrator-dispatch paths send only the caller input); `output_schema` is documentary (Cycle 6 WP-D). Single-agent ensembles with no `system_prompt` (claim-extractor, text-summarizer) run with no format contract at all. Run 2 shows qwen3:8b complies once the contract is in the prompt → a contract-delivery gap, not a capability gap. This contradicts the claim-extractor YAML's assumption that `default_task` shapes output, so it reopens the Cycle 6 WP-E documentary-contract decision.
- **D2b — deliverable form (DECIDE).** code-generator's agents carry system_prompts asking for client-readable markdown ("Format code with appropriate fenced blocks"; "Output exactly what the client should see") — the model obeys, but the form targets a human reader, not a bare file a `write` consumes. The irreducible I/O-contract question (carry-forward #3).

**Disposition (practitioner, 2026-06-02).** DECIDE on the I/O-contract (D2a + D2b); the D1 extraction fix is shaped to the DECIDE outcome. Loop-back #2: BUILD → DECIDE.

## BUILD-surfaced finding: client-tool-action terminal gap (2026-05-24)

**What surfaced.** At the WP-A BUILD reflection gate, the handler swap made concrete that ADR-027's pipeline emits only `ContentDelta` + `Completion` — the chat-completions surface now **never** returns `finish_reason: "tool_calls"`. The practitioner's north-star is: use OpenCode to invoke the RDD skill, with the actual work (writing files to the *local* machine, running commands) **delegated to ensembles**. The only coherent mechanism for "ensemble does the work, file lands on the local machine":

1. OpenCode sends a request carrying its client tools (`write_file`, `bash`, `read`).
2. The endpoint dispatches the generation to an ensemble (e.g., `code-generator` produces file content).
3. The endpoint returns the deliverable to OpenCode **as a `tool_calls` response** (`write_file(path, content=<ensemble output>)`).
4. OpenCode executes its local tool and writes to the developer's machine.
5. The loop continues (OpenCode returns the tool result; the endpoint decides the next step).

Ensembles run server-side and write to `.llm-orc/agentic-sessions/`, **disjoint** from the developer's filesystem (essay E4.2.1; PLAY note 22). So the deliverable must return through the client's local tools — the endpoint must emit `tool_calls`. ADR-027's pipeline has no stage that does this and is single-turn (no agentic loop).

**Diagnosis — how the cycle missed it (not a clarity failure on the practitioner's part):**

- **C1 conflation.** The cycle framed its problem as "NL-routing-to-ensembles ≈ 0 under tool-rich clients" and treated *both* direct-completion *and* client-tool-delegation as the failure. That conflated (a) the orchestrator *avoiding* ensemble dispatch (the real problem) with (b) client-tool-calls as the *mechanism* for applying work to the local filesystem (a needed capability). ADR-027 fixed (a) by removing the orchestrator-LLM, which killed (b) as a side effect.
- **ADR-022 §line 48 already described the split it dropped:** *"client-declared tools remain correct for actions on the tool-user's filesystem... when the user asks to write code, `code-generator` covers it."* That is the two-step flow (ensemble generates, client tool writes); ADR-027 dropped the second half without replacement.
- **No Cycle 7 spike tested the real-client round-trip.** Cycle 6 γ/λ ran against real clients but tested the *orchestrator-LLM* (the thing being removed); note 22 and λ.5-paid were literally the dispatch→client-write handoff failing. The Cycle 7 pipeline spikes (ζ/ε/ε'/μ/ν) ran against Python harnesses producing text — never through OpenCode. **The architecture being kept was never run through the client it exists to serve.**
- **The scope-of-claim partition covered routing + synthesis, never delivery-to-client.** No essay node named the client-tool-application surface, so no audit (5-round research, 7-round DECIDE) could catch its absence. The DISCOVER "rapid compounding" snapshot warning pointed at this risk.

**What still holds.** AS-9 (structurally-bounded roles produce reliable output) and AS-10 (capability matching from request content alone) are unaffected. ADR-027's architecture is **incomplete, not wrong**: it built the answer-a-question terminal but not the do-work-on-the-client terminal. The fix is *aligned* with ADR-027's philosophy — a framework that *deterministically* wraps an ensemble deliverable into a client tool-call would be more reliable than the orchestrator-LLM that failed at it (note 22).

**WP-A disposition.** WP-A stands as committed (`e538264` + `0a7a822`) — a faithful, green, reversible increment of ADR-027 as written. The `ClientToolCall` chunk plumbing removed in `0a7a822` (handler + `_collect_non_streaming` branches + `_build_completion_body` tool_calls shaping) comes back cleanly when the pipeline gains a client-tool-action stage; the `OrchestratorChunk` union still includes `ClientToolCall`.

## Path forward (loop-back BUILD → RESEARCH, 2026-05-24)

The next learning point is empirical, so RESEARCH re-entry leads with a validation spike (ADR-087 validation-spike-as-research; the cycle's own method).

**Spike (next session) — OpenCode client-tool round-trip.** Question it must answer: *can a framework-driven pipeline hand a real OpenCode session a `tool_calls` response carrying an ensemble deliverable, have OpenCode execute it locally, and close the multi-turn loop?* Minimal shape:
- Stand up agentic-serving (or a minimal stand-in) that, on a capability-matched request, dispatches to an ensemble (e.g., `code-generator`) and returns `finish_reason: "tool_calls"` with a `write_file` call carrying the deliverable.
- Point a real OpenCode session at it. Observe: does OpenCode execute the synthesized tool-call against the local filesystem? Does it send the tool result back? Does the next turn route correctly?
- Sub-questions: where does the target path come from (planner? request?); how does a deliverable map to a client tool (`code-generator` → `write_file`; what about `bash`/test-runs?); is deterministic emission reliable where the orchestrator-LLM failed (note 22)?
- Free-tier local Ollama + a real OpenCode install; ~$0 (confirm before any paid step per `feedback_free_options_preference`).

**After the spike (sketch only — detail deferred to what the spike teaches):**
1. RESEARCH: fold finding + spike result into an Essay-Outline 006 amendment naming the client-tool-action terminal as a first-order surface (re-audit per Essay-Outline-as-checkpoint).
2. DISCOVER (update mode): make the "delegate work, apply locally" loop explicit in the Skill Orchestration User + Tool User mental models; assumption-inversion on "endpoint-returns-text is sufficient."
3. DECIDE: amend ADR-027 (client-tool-action disposition + multi-turn loop) or new ADR; new scenarios + interaction-specs.
4. ARCHITECT: pipeline gains a terminal stage (deliverable → client tool-call); planner + synthesizer roles adjust; re-wire the streaming/non-streaming `tool_calls` surface.
5. BUILD: re-introduce `ClientToolCall` emission; build the new terminal; then WP-B/WP-C against the corrected surface.

**Do NOT resume WP-B/WP-C** until the terminal shape is settled — they build the routing-planner + synthesizer for the text-only terminal, which the finding shows is half the surface.

## Spike candidates for Cycle 7

To be ordered after RESEARCH establishes the question shape, but pre-named for orientation:

- **Spike ε:** minimal routing-planner ensemble + response-synthesizer ensemble + Python harness for end-to-end plan→dispatch→synthesize pipeline. Run against the prompts that broke under orchestrator-LLM routing.
- **Spike ζ:** routing-planner reliability — JSON-output adherence across prompt shapes, including adversarial / ambiguous prompts. Tests the cheap-tier-model-as-structured-output assumption.
- **Spike η:** synthesizer behavior on multi-dispatch results — does the narrower role + structured input prevent the confabulation pattern the orchestrator-LLM exhibited?
- **Spike θ:** general-completion fallback ensemble shape — does wrapping direct completion in an ensemble degrade response quality (compared to note 1 / note 18 quality on the string-reverse task)?
- **Spike ι:** schema-as-enforcement reliability — does qwen3:8b produce schema-conformant JSON when retried with feedback after non-conformant output?
- **Spike κ (alternative-architecture):** `tool_choice` constrained decoding probe under Zen + MiniMax M2.5 — does Zen support the parameter? Does the model honor it? Latency + reliability shape?
- **Spike μ (MODEL-boundary; ran 2026-05-22):** confabulation-mode generalization — tests whether Spike ε ε.1's structural-bounding finding generalizes from PLAY note 22 to three other documented confabulation modes. Free-tier; $0 cost; ~3 min wall-clock. Findings: μ.1 path hallucination transforms (confident-specific fabrication → honest-generic-conventions with explicit hedging); μ.2 substrate-path-as-deliverable structurally avoided (text-only synthesizer surface); μ.3 coherent factual errors uncalibrated bounded by Rule 1 + Rule 5. Extended combined audit depth to 4 confabulation modes + 13 tests at qwen3:8b. Writeup at `essays/research-logs/cycle-7-spike-mu-confabulation-generalization.md`. Practitioner-authorized AS-9 codification followed.

## Feed-Forward Signals

### From Cycle 7 loop-back #8 — Spike π form/adequacy gate (DECIDE CLOSED at gate 2026-06-12; ADR-041 drafted+audited; BUILD next)

1. **Procedural NEXT — BUILD entry.** DECIDE loop-back #8 is CLOSED (gate note `.rdd/gates/cycle-7-loopback8-decide-build-gate.md`). The amendment became a **new ADR-041** (Destination-Validity Gate, extending ADR-035 — the corpus successor convention, NOT an in-place ADR-035 amendment). Argument audit converged R2; conformance scan done; downstream blocks (domain-model #21 / scenarios / interaction-specs) landed; snapshot No Grounding Reframe; **ARCHITECT skip practitioner-confirmed**. `**In-progress phase:** build` now holds. **BUILD = de-gate + FormGate-seam install per `conformance-scan-cycle-7-loopback8.md`** (10 BUILD-work items + 2 test-gap violations). Pending: the DECIDE-close commit (docs + Spike π code/data, practitioner go) before BUILD code changes.

2. **What the amendment encodes (spike-grounded).** A three-layer escalation: (a) **deterministic destination-validity gate** at the FormGate seam — the protection floor, both seams' deterministic slice (form bleed + intent divergence), tier-independent; confirmed live (0 invalid files reached the client across 5 gated sessions vs 3/5 baseline). (b) **cheap-tier server-side recovery** (re-dispatch on refusal) — rescues intermittent bleeds, bounded by a retry cap. (c) **coder-tier escalation** (ADR-014 Calibration Gate cheap→escalated) for the persistent residual (Arm E: MiniMax 6/6 vs 8b 3/6). Semantic "parses-but-wrong" residual stays PLAY's. Discharges the ADR-035 Conditional Acceptance form-seam. Directly answers #7-tail signal 1 (ADR-035 form/coherence was named the next limit).

3. **BUILD seed committed (env-gated).** `41296f3` carries `_spike_pi_recover` (loop_driver) + the `artifact_store` wiring; `bae2ecf` carries `_spike_pi_form_check` (artifact_bridge) — all gated on `LLMORC_SPIKE_PI_GATE=parse`, additive, inert by default. **BUILD de-gates:** install the parse-check at the FormGate seam properly, thread `destination_path` through `marshal` as a permanent signature, make the 2-retry cap a config value, drop the `LLMORC_SPIKE_PI_GATE` gate + the SPIKE-π comments. **Open BUILD design choice:** wire coder-tier escalation on cap-exhaustion (the Arm-E lever) into the recovery, or leave it an operator-config tier default.

4. **The recovery cap is a real limit, not a bug.** The 2-retry cap exhausts on persistent cheap-coder bleeds (Cell B runs 3/4 ended short, protected-not-converged) — the designed protect-but-not-recover floor. The lever is coder capability (Arm E), not a higher cap alone (3 generations of a ~50%-bleed coder still fails ~1/8). The amendment should name the cap a tunable and escalation the real fix, not promise the cheap tier converges everything.

5. **Measurement discipline.** "All-files-valid over *produced* files" reads vacuously for short sessions (a gate-refused session scores all-valid on its 1-3 files). Score **converged-and-valid** (present5 AND all_valid). Relevant to the ADR's scenarios and any BUILD acceptance gate.

6. **Harness lesson reconfirmed (extends #7-tail signal 4).** The session-id collision (identical prompt → `sha256(first message)` collision → shared action record) bit the live arm again; the fix is a unique per-session prompt marker (now in `run_live_arm.sh`). Any future live battery reusing one serve process must vary the prompt or restart serve per session.

7. **Protection = structure/quality-separation (the north-star framing, gate-settled).** ADR-041 centers protection on *keeping the structure/quality boundary legible*, not on sparing the user a bad diff (the client's permission gate already does that). The gate guarantees whatever reaches the client is structurally valid, so any remaining failure is unambiguously ensemble-quality — the only thing the north star says should remain. BUILD/PLAY framing carries this: a short session that says "structure delivered, this destination needs a better coder" is the legible floor; a broken file is not. The routing-signal reading is a *consequence*, not a competitor.

8. **Escalation ladder: deterministic trigger, opt-in ceiling (practitioner, gate).** The ladder is **cheap → less-cheap → frontier** coder tiers (ADR-014). Free-local rungs may escalate deterministically on a persistent-bleed signal; the **frontier rung crosses a cost boundary → opt-in** (configured at a layer or consented before a run), with a **local-degradation path** (no opt-in → cap at the best free rung → honest short session). BUILD wires the ADR-014 lever with this opt-in/cost-gate, NOT an automatic frontier escalation. Preserves the free-first standard ([[feedback_free_options_preference]]).

9. **North-star target = a long-horizon RDD-like flow → axis-2 is the PLAY target (practitioner, gate).** The north star is a sustained multi-step RDD-like flow, not a single 5-file trajectory. The gate+recovery are validated only single-trajectory (n=5×2). PLAY/first-deployment validates: (a) does the structure/quality separation stay legible over a long flow; (b) the recovery cap's behaviour across many turns; (c) convergence-under-escalation in a *wired* session (Arm E was isolated, n=6). Two snapshot feed-forward items ride here: instrument the recovered-case ADR-040 completeness trace on the first live session (P3-N2); treat the routing-signal/short-session experience as a first-session observation target.

### From Cycle 7 loop-back #7 tail — Spike η / ADR-040 (closed 2026-06-10)

1. **The completeness question is settled; the next real limit is deliverable COHERENCE + FORM, not completeness.** ADR-039 (content anchor) and ADR-040 (deterministic completeness gate, named-file-grounded) are both done. η's live runs surfaced the residual concretely: a session converged with all five files but built the CLI as `index.js` (JavaScript for a Python library — intent-divergence; the gate counts deliverables, it does not validate coherence), and the 8b `cli.py` carried a trailing prose paragraph → SyntaxError (an ADR-035 form-gate bleed). North-star parity on the file-action subset now turns on deliverable coherence + form, owned by **ADR-035 + capability-ensemble quality**, not by the framework's control decisions. This is where the next BUILD/PLAY attention should go.

2. **Arm B (enumerate → deterministic gate, persist-once) is a recorded, buildable fallback — with a named trigger.** ADR-040's scope is grounded, not closed-forever. If a future cycle finds a task space that is implicit/compaction-heavy AND where the judge demonstrably false-COMPLETEs AND the enumerator demonstrably beats it (arm C validated enumeration only on *described* deliverables, never vague "production-ready X"), build arm B. Prior art: arm C feasibility (recall 0.967/1.000 on qwen3:8b) + the eval/retry analysis (concentrating stochasticity into one turn-1 chokepoint makes it verifiable via consensus / structural rules / reconciliation-against-produced, and retriable cheaply and reversibly — unlike the per-turn judge whose wrong verdict is irreversible under the real client). η log §"Spike η resolution" + ADR-040.

3. **Latent multi-tenancy concern for the single-turn surface (WP-B/C/D): session identity = `sha256(first user message)`.** Two clients sending an identical first message resolve to the same session and share its in-memory action record (`session_registry.resolve_identity`). η's test harness hit this directly as state-bleed across headless runs. It does not affect the per-conversation file-action loop (the first message is unique per real task), but any multi-client / single-turn-surface hardening should revisit identity derivation. Recorded in ADR-040 §Spike η resolution + the gate note.

4. **Test-harness discipline for multi-session live batteries:** identical prompts collide on the sha256 session id and the in-memory action record never cleans up between headless `opencode run` invocations, bleeding produced-file state across runs (it briefly read as a 3/4 judge false-COMPLETE before the artifact was caught). Vary the prompt per run (the η fix: a unique inert suffix) or restart serve per run (the σ approach). Any future live battery that reuses one serve process must do one of these.

5. **Methodological reinforcement (live-primary, sharpened).** The isolated judge probe (0/12) and an easy clean-live case (4/4) *agreed* that the judge was fine — and that agreement was misleading; only a deliberate break-the-judge probe found the adequacy is conditional on explicit enumeration, and only an architecture check found the dramatic compaction break (6/6) is structurally non-manifest here. Lesson for future gates: when an isolated probe and an easy live case agree, that is not robustness — stress-test the hard shapes, and check whether the dramatic failures are even architecturally reachable before acting on them. Strengthens [[live-multiturn-primary-spike]] + [[determinism-over-carve-outs]] (the memory was refined: grounding a boundary can resolve to "keep the stochastic fallback" — but only after it is tried-and-not-broken, not asserted).

6. **Cycle-close items carried (not new this tail):** the system-design / ORIENTATION / field-guide current-state sweep (deferred since WP-LB-A — stale across the whole loop-back surface, needs one consolidated pass at cycle close); WP-LB-E (wrapper-contingency seam); the single-turn surface WP-B/C/D; the cycle-close field-guide batch.

### From Cycle 7 loop-back BUILD — WP-LB-I close + Spike ψ″ (2026-06-04)

1. **DECIDE loop-back #5 entry package:** Finding F section above + research logs (ψ log §Spike ψ″ pre-registration/run/verdict + E4; WP validation log §WP-LB-I built + validated) + artifacts (`scratch/wp-lb-i-smoke/`, `scratch/spike-psi-prime-prime-should-finish/`). The question is well-posed: where does session termination live? The evidence gives clean separations on both sides of F-ψ″.3.
2. **Belief-map the termination-policy pole.** Framework-level termination is the thesis-consistent move (single-step enforcement, directive presence, batch-truncation all resolved that way) — which is exactly why the loop-back #3 discipline applies: examine conditional-composition and restructured-text against it on named criteria, not by pattern-rhyme default.
2a. **Post-session reframe (candidate material, practitioner-discussed 2026-06-05):** the ψ″ data shows the model's own stopping judgment is mostly sound — E2 stopped 10/10 (work done, no guidance) and E4a continued 6/10 (work remaining, no guidance); the guidance *overrides* that judgment rather than informing it. The guidance is needed to shape *how* the model continues (delegate, not inline), not *whether*. This adds a fourth candidate: **two-call composition** — trailing turns first ask the seat-filler continue-vs-stop without guidance (the measured-sound judgment); only a continue answer triggers a second, guidance-composed call to shape the work into delegation. Built from two separately-measured behaviors; costs one extra local call on continuing turns; the second call's context shape is unmeasured (needs a probe arm; ψ.4c tool-list constraint binds any retry composition). Protocol constraint for all candidates: the model IS the stop mechanism — OpenCode ends the loop on a no-tool-calls response, so every path must produce a clean text-only turn; no client-side stop lever exists. Probe shapes: each candidate gets a cheap ψ″-harness arm (the E-arm pattern) before the ADR commits; E3's negative already bounds the appended-clause variant.

The soak-distortion point rides with this: do not read the ADR-036 ≥0.9 soak until termination is fixed — Finding F inflates the numerator's turn stream.
4. **ψ″ harness is reusable for DECIDE-entry probes.** The E-arm pattern (real capture bytes; composition via the landed code path, byte-verified) plus the fidelity-check discipline transfers directly to any mechanism probe. E3's negative bounds the wording lever cheaply.

6. **Client-invisibility has no dedicated test** — it holds structurally (guidance exists only on the framework → seat-filler hop). Candidate cheap test if the composition is touched again in loop-back #5 BUILD.
