### From Cycle 7 loop-back BUILD — Spike φ + Finding D disposition (DECIDE loop-back #2, 2026-06-02)

1. **DECIDE scope = the client-tool deliverable I/O-contract (D2a + D2b).** Spike φ established Finding D is three separable layers (D1 extraction / D2a contract-delivery / D2b deliverable form). Practitioner disposition: DECIDE on D2a + D2b; D1's extraction fix is shaped to the outcome (so it does not pre-commit a shape DECIDE might override — F-φ.3 sequencing). The DECIDE question: *what should a capability ensemble emit when its deliverable becomes a client-tool argument (a `write` body / a `bash` command), and how does that contract reach and constrain the model?*

2. **D2a reopens a specific Cycle 6 call — read it before drafting.** The claim-extractor / text-summarizer YAML comments record the Cycle 6 WP-E decision to keep `output_schema` + `default_task` **documentary** (per Spike β: "drift is upstream at the orchestrator's input.data override, not the synthesizer's compliance"). That reasoning presupposed `default_task` *reaches* the model and shapes output. Spike φ Run 1 (no contract → chatty) + the grep-proven zero runtime reads of `default_task` say it does **not** reach the model at all. So the DECIDE re-examines Cycle 6 WP-E with corrected evidence. **Caveat to confirm at DECIDE:** zero-reads is grep-strong and two execution paths were traced (MCP-invoke; orchestrator dispatch `orchestrator_tool_dispatch.py:717-720,766-769`), but DECIDE should confirm no path was missed before treating "default_task is inert" as settled.

3. **Grounding already in hand — the cheap model is contract-capable (Run 2).** qwen3:8b complied exactly with the claim-extractor format contract once it was in the prompt. This narrows the D2 mechanism space: the *format-compliance* flavor (D2a) may not need heavy reject-and-retry enforcement — getting a well-formed contract to the model may suffice. The hard part is D2b (defining bare-file vs human-readable form). Mechanism options the cycle has pre-named: `output_schema`-as-enforcement (reject-and-retry); a `submit_file`-shaped synthesizer (agent calls a tool whose param is the bare content); a deterministic post-agent shaper; or simply wiring `default_task` through to the agent prompt (the D2a minimal fix). **Caveat:** Run 2 is n=1 paragraph / one ensemble / one local model — compliance breadth across prompts/ensembles/escalated tiers is unmeasured (a DECIDE-entry or BUILD probe candidate).

4. **D1 carries an internal where-sub-fork (BUILD gate, do not pre-decide).** Envelope-side terminal-node extraction relies on `results` insertion order (robust for linear pipelines, fragile for branching DAGs); executor-side populating a canonical deliverable field in `finalize_result` (where `depends_on` is known) is the robust alternative. Surface at the BUILD scenario-group gate when D1 lands.

5. **Connects to the cycle's standing form-drift carry-forward #3.** Finding D D2b *is* carry-forward #3 (claim-extractor non-conformance) demonstrated on the code-generator → client-`write` path. The DECIDE ADR on I/O-contract enforcement the cycle has flagged since DECIDE-first-pass (and Cycle 6) is the natural home. Check ADR-024 (`output_schema`) + ADR-025 (substrate-write) + the ADR-027 scope when drafting.

### From Cycle 7 loop-back BUILD — WP-LB-G seat-filler delegation + Finding D (landed 2026-06-02 evening)

**WP-LB-G landed (commit offers the seat-filler `invoke_ensemble` + the capability list + delegation guidance; `LoopDriver.decide` augments the tool list, `get_loop_driver` threads `_build_capability_names`). Suite 2891 green.** This closes Finding B at the mechanism level.

1. **DELEGATION FIRES — Finding B resolved (validated against the real model).** Re-ran the real-OpenCode rig (real `llm-orc serve` + qwen3:14b, $0). The serve log shows the cheap seat-filler **chose to delegate**: `tool-call emit: tool=invoke_ensemble` → `dispatch start: ensemble=code-generator` → `tier selection: topaz_skill=code_generation` → artifact written → bridge marshalled → `finish_reason: tool_calls` with a `write`. The full callee → bridge → ApplyWork chain is reachable end-to-end with a real model. The cheap-driver-skips-delegation tension did not bite (the nudge held); cross-prompt/cross-client reliability is an axis-2 / PLAY observation. WP-LB-G met its acceptance gate.

2. **CRITICAL FINDING D (new blocker) — the marshalled deliverable is the raw ensemble result envelope, not usable file content.** The `write` content was `{"results": {"coder": {"response": "…```python\ndef fibonacci…```\n### Key Points…"}}}`. The bridge faithfully marshalled what was stored; the problem is upstream at the **ADR-025 substrate-write / ensemble-output-contract layer**. Two layers: **D1 (extraction)** — the artifact holds the full multi-agent `{"results": {coder, critic, synthesizer}}` dict, not the synthesizer's final output; **D2 (form drift)** — even the synthesizer output is conversational markdown (prose + fenced code), not bare file content. This is the cycle's recorded form-drift / I/O-contract concern (carry-forward #3; claim-extractor non-conformance) demonstrated for code-generator → client-write. Evidence: `scratch/wp-lb-c-opencode-validation/wplbg_stored_artifact.json` + `serve_wplbg.log`.

3. **NEXT: Finding D disposition (DECIDE-adjacent).** D1 looks like a deliverable-extraction bug (the artifact should hold the synthesizer's output, not the raw result dict). D2 is the I/O-contract / form-drift design question the cycle flagged for a DECIDE-level policy (bare-deliverable contract for client-tool content — `output_schema` / a `submit_file`-shaped synthesizer / a deterministic shaper). **A natural fresh-context boundary** — Finding D is upstream of the terminal surface WP-LB-C/G worked in. WP-LB-E (wrapper seam) / WP-LB-F (axis-2 instrumentation) remain after Finding D. Research log: `essays/research-logs/cycle-7-wp-lb-c-opencode-validation.md` §"Update — WP-LB-G".

### From Cycle 7 loop-back BUILD — WP-LB-C Client-Tool-Action Terminal + real-OpenCode validation (landed 2026-06-02)

**WP-LB-C landed (commits `f32bada` layer-map debt fix; `aa971a1` refactor extract Terminal + Loop Driver `decide()`; `272997e` feat bridge wiring; `ab07eb7` feat non-streaming `tool_calls`; `24e6100` test real-ASGI round-trip; `33a65ac` docs OpenCode smoke procedure; `8e63cee` fix seat-filler `base_url`). Suite 2888 green.** The Client-Tool-Action Terminal (`agentic/client_tool_action_terminal.py`, L3) is the `_ChatCompletionsCaller` for the tool-driven surface — the practitioner chose the architecture-faithful split (Terminal owns emission + the bridge call; Loop Driver `decide()` returns a `TurnOutcome` and owns the per-turn choice/dispatch). Streaming + non-streaming `tool_calls` emission; substrate-routed deliverables marshalled to full fidelity via the Artifact Bridge (degrades to a dispatch-failure completion on bridge error / binary deliverable).

1. **NORTH-STAR VALIDATION RAN against real OpenCode (the practitioner's "don't fly blind" directive, discharged).** Real OpenCode 1.15.5 (headless) → real `llm-orc serve` (WP-LB-C terminal) → real qwen3:14b seat-filler → `finish_reason: tool_calls` → **OpenCode executed the `write` locally, `hello.py` landed, loop closed with parity.** FC-47/48/50 validated against the real client, $0 local Ollama. The WP-A scar ("never run through the client") is closed at the real-client layer for the terminal/loop-participation mechanism. Research log: `essays/research-logs/cycle-7-wp-lb-c-opencode-validation.md`; artifacts retained at `scratch/wp-lb-c-opencode-validation/`.

2. **CRITICAL FINDING B (open) — the seat-filler is never offered `invoke_ensemble`, so ensemble delegation does NOT fire end-to-end.** `LoopDriver.decide` passes only the client's tools (`write`/`edit`/`bash`/`read`) to the seat-filler; nothing augments the list with `invoke_ensemble`. So a real seat-filler can only grounded-carry (emit a literal client tool call) or finish — it cannot delegate. **Evidence:** the OpenCode run produced **zero ensemble dispatches and zero artifacts**; the cheap seat-filler generated the code itself. **Consequence:** the callee → bridge → ApplyWork machinery (WP-LB-B FC-44, WP-LB-D bridge, WP-LB-C substrate marshalling) is correct + harness-tested but **unreachable in production** — the harness tests pass only because they *script* `invoke_ensemble`. The cycle's central value proposition (delegate work to ensembles) is not wired. **Deeper tension:** the seat-filler decides whether to delegate, and a model capable enough to drive is often capable enough to skip delegation (qwen3:14b did) — the flip side of the recorded over-delegation worry; only a real run with `invoke_ensemble` offered can answer whether/when it delegates.

3. **NEXT: WP-LB-G (proposed) — offer the seat-filler `invoke_ensemble` + the capability list, before WP-LB-E/F.** WP-LB-E (wrapper-contingency seam) and WP-LB-F (axis-2 instrumentation) are both downstream of delegation working at all; sequence WP-LB-G first. The *design* is settled (ADR-033 callee + `invoke_ensemble`; WP-D `_build_capability_names` is reusable) — the gap is integration + a delegation-vs-act-directly system prompt. **Load-bearing acceptance gate:** a real OpenCode session whose serve log shows a real `invoke_ensemble` dispatch + a `code-generator` artifact marshalled through the bridge into the client write (not a scripted test). **Loop-back trigger:** if the real run shows the seat-filler will not reliably delegate, loop back to DECIDE on the delegation-decision mechanism (`tool_choice` forcing / routing pre-filter / different driver-vs-delegation split) — on evidence, not speculation.

4. **Finding C (minor, known) — seat-filler tool-calling is prompt-sensitive (thinking-mode).** One probe returned no tool call; an explicit prompt returned `tool_calls` reliably. Consistent with "seat-filler behavior unverified in BUILD by design" (axis-2 / PLAY concern), not a defect.

### From Cycle 7 loop-back BUILD — WP-LB-D Artifact Bridge + read_deliverable (landed 2026-06-02)

1. **WP-LB-D landed: the deliverable-content marshalling step is built.** `SessionArtifactStore.read_deliverable(reference) -> str | bytes` (commit `2b7f362` — the first read-side API on the formerly write-only store; structural inverse of the write path [strip `agentic-sessions/` prefix, rejoin under root]; decode-probe str/bytes; `ArtifactNotFoundError` [`LlmOrcStructuralError`, `error_kind="artifact_not_found"`, `operator_intervention_required`] on unresolvable reference) + `agentic/artifact_bridge.py` `ArtifactBridge.marshal(envelope)` (commit `3b9d829` — owns the artifact-vs-inline branch; substrate → `read_deliverable` with fidelity, inline → `envelope.primary` no-op; reconstructs the typed `ArtifactReference` from the serialized `envelope.artifacts[0]` dict) + integration suite (commit `af5af7d` — real bridge↔store; **FC-49 fidelity-at-scale gate**: a >256 KB multi-byte UTF-8 deliverable round-trips byte-identical; retention-window lifecycle case [`cleanup_session` disposal → stale ref raises `ArtifactNotFoundError`]). Suite 2873 green; Tier-1 stewardship clean.

2. **Built in isolation, NOT yet wired into the live loop (deliberate; WP-LB-C wires it).** `loop_driver._deliverable_text` still reads `envelope.primary` directly — the bridge is the *capability* to close the substrate-deliverable-fidelity gap, consumed by the Client-Tool-Action Terminal (WP-LB-C), which ADR-034 names as the bridge's consumer. The live gap (substrate-routed deliverable marshalling the summary instead of the content) closes when WP-LB-C wires terminal → bridge. WP-LB-D respects scope: the terminal does not exist yet, so the bridge is tested against fixtures + the real store.

3. **NORTH-STAR VALIDATION DIRECTIVE (practitioner, at WP-LB-D gate): don't fly blind — validate against real OpenCode at the earliest runnable point.** BUILD tests (incl. WP-LB-D) validate *mechanism*, not the north star; the north-star validation proper is a real OpenCode session against a real `llm-orc serve`. The cycle's own WP-A scar tissue ("the architecture being kept was never run through the client it exists to serve") is the failure mode to avoid repeating. **The earliest a parity round-trip becomes runnable is after WP-LB-C** (terminal emits `tool_calls` + loop participation; TS-12), NOT PLAY. **Carry into WP-LB-C:** (a) add a real-serving-surface integration test (drive the actual ASGI chat-completions endpoint with a tool-carrying request + `role:"tool"` follow-up, assert real `tool_calls` SSE carrying bridge-marshalled content), not just loop-driver fixtures; (b) surface a $0 real-OpenCode smoke-test procedure for the practitioner to run (real OpenCode + local Ollama, per memory `free-options-preference`); treat the real-client round-trip as a first-class WP-LB-C acceptance gate. Axis-2 long-horizon coherence remains PLAY/first-deployment by design (ADR-033 §6b, ADR-097). Recorded durably as memory `validate-against-real-client-not-harness`.

4. **Next: WP-LB-C** (Client-Tool-Action Terminal + multi-turn loop participation) — both hard prereqs satisfied (WP-LB-B + WP-LB-D landed; Track A-LB.1 done). Re-introduce `ClientToolCall` emission (the `0a7a822` removal: handler branch + `_collect_non_streaming` branch + `_build_completion_body` `tool_calls` shaping + the `tool_calls` field on `_NonStreamingResult`), wire terminal → `ArtifactBridge` → `write` tool call, consume `role:"tool"` follow-ups into the loop-driver (`_extract_request` currently drops `role:"tool"` messages — the loop-participation gap). Then WP-LB-E (delegation-target strategy seam) + WP-LB-F (`TurnDecision` surfacing).

### From Cycle 7 loop-back BUILD — WP-LB-B Loop Driver + Single-Step Enforcer (landed 2026-06-02)

1. **WP-LB-B landed: the layer-A control structure is built.** `single_step_enforcer.py` (FC-43 batch-truncation), `loop_driver.py` (FC-44 callee / FC-45 grounded carry / FC-51 TurnDecision), and the `get_loop_driver()` swap (real driver + Model-Profile seat-filler resolution, FC-42 event assertion). Suite 2865 green; Tier-1 stewardship clean; callee boundary integration-verified against the real Tool Dispatch. Commits `67d42b9`/`81ad0ea`/`813823e`/`fd0e74f`/`b16252f`/`15bf81d` + amendment `782b092`.

2. **Seat-filler contract = Reading B (Design Amendment #13).** The seat-filler emits either a **literal client tool call** (passed through verbatim — grounded carry, FC-45) or an **`invoke_ensemble`** internal call (callee generation, FC-44; the driver dispatches one ensemble and maps the deliverable to a client tool). This was a BUILD-design-gate decision: the implicit ARCHITECT reading (driver intercepts every `write`/`edit` and regenerates content via an ensemble) would route an observed/literal value through ensemble regeneration and lose grounding fidelity. Provenance is design-phase allocation; `invoke_ensemble` is the established ADR-003 delegation primitive. **Downstream implication:** WP-LB-C's terminal and WP-LB-D's bridge build on Reading B — the deliverable they marshal is what the seat-filler's `invoke_ensemble` decision produced, not a driver-intercepted write.

3. **AXIS-2 MITIGATION CANDIDATE (PLAY watch-list): a driver-state / plan artifact for long-horizon coherence.** Reading B added a new per-turn judgment the cheap seat-filler must make — `invoke_ensemble`-vs-literal-client-tool — on top of the trajectory-coherence burden axis-2 already names (OQ #27 axis 2). A WP-LB-B gate exchange surfaced an artifact-based mitigation, echoing single-step enforcement's "make it structural, not a model assumption" move: a **durable driver-maintained plan/scratchpad artifact** (re-read at the top of each turn from the `SessionArtifactStore`, ADR-025) externalizes "task / done / next" so the cheap driver re-grounds structurally instead of holding the whole trajectory in a compacting context. It folds naturally into the **deferred `todowrite` surface** (ADR-033 §6c; signal #6 below) — OpenCode's client-side `todowrite` is this mechanism. **Honest scope:** (a) it buys *coherence* (driver stays self-consistent) but not *correctness* — the plan is still cheap-model-generated, so it converts "drift" into "committed-to-a-wrong-plan," a distinct FC-51 signature (a bad early `TurnDecision` faithfully executed vs. turn-to-turn wandering); (b) it does NOT directly address the internal-vs-client tool-class pick (that lever is tool-surface shaping, which tangles with grounded carry). **Disposition: NOT built — recorded as the leading axis-2 mitigation candidate.** Per ADR-033 Conditional Acceptance the axis-2 risk is a PLAY/first-deployment validation target; FC-51 `TurnDecision` instrumentation is designed to reveal *which* failure signature appears, which decides the response (plan-artifact for coherence drift / tool-surface change for wrong tool-class / frontier-driver swap for raw capability). **PLAY should instrument the axis-2 run to distinguish coherence-drift (committed-wrong-plan) from turn-to-turn wandering, so the right mitigation is chosen on evidence, not pre-built.** Pursuing it = a follow-on ADR + WP (driver-state artifact, possibly folding in `todowrite`), not a WP-LB-B/C/D change.

4. **Deliverable-content fidelity is a WP-LB-D gap, not closed in WP-LB-B.** `loop_driver._deliverable_text` reads `envelope.primary` — for substrate-routed capability ensembles (ADR-025) that is a summary + `ArtifactReference`, not the content. WP-LB-D's Artifact Bridge (`read_deliverable`) resolves full content. The callee integration test verifies structural flow (real dispatch accepts the `invoke_ensemble` arg shape; deliverable reaches a client `write`), explicitly NOT large-deliverable fidelity (Acceptance Criteria Table row 3 — WP-LB-D).

5. **`_resolve_seat_filler` is the swappable seam (FC-46) and the PLAY lever.** The seat-filler resolves the orchestrator's `model_profile` → tool-calling `ModelInterface` via `ModelFactory`, guarded on `supports_tool_calling`. Swapping cheap-tier ↔ frontier-tier (the named axis-2 fallback) is a profile config edit, no Loop Driver change. End-to-end seat-filler behavior is unverified in BUILD by design — it is the PLAY/first-deployment axis-2 run (a real OpenCode session), per ADR-033 §6b. The factory test overrides this seam; no real model call in BUILD.

### From Cycle 7 loop-back BUILD — WP-LB-A surface-mode discrimination (landed 2026-06-02, `4d8108d`)

1. **WP-LB-A landed.** The Serving-Layer surface-mode discriminator (`_is_tool_driven`, `len(request.tools) > 0`) branches tool-driven requests to `get_loop_driver()` and non-tool requests to `get_dispatch_pipeline()`; both satisfy `_ChatCompletionsCaller` so the heartbeat/sink/streaming lifecycle is caller-agnostic. WP-LB-A ships a `_StubLoopDriver` (finishes with a stop completion — the safe terminal) behind the `get_loop_driver` factory; **WP-LB-B swaps the factory body for the real `agentic/loop_driver.py` with no call-site change.** Suite 2851 green; mypy strict + ruff + format clean; 4 new tests in `TestSurfaceModeDiscrimination`.

2. **FC-42 partially verified at WP-LB-A; event-assertion deferred to WP-LB-B.** The routing behavior + per-request mutual-exclusivity are verified via observable response content (distinguishable stub callers). FC-42's *specified* verification is event-based (`tools[]` → `TurnDecision`; no-tools → `PlanEmitted`); neither event exists until WP-LB-B (TurnDecision) and a real pipeline (PlanEmitted). The event-type assertion is the natural WP-LB-B addition against real callers — do not fake it against stubs.

3. **NORTH-STAR IMPLICATION — the four RDD modes map to both layers; axis-2 concentrates in artifact-reasoning + code-recovery, NOT the conversational path (sharpens WP-LB-B).** *(Corrected 2026-06-02 after practitioner challenge: an earlier draft of this signal over-indexed on RDD-is-conversational; RDD is conversation **plus** artifact generation, reasoning across artifacts, and code work.)* The north-star process is RDD-via-OpenCode, whose turns all carry `tools[]` (→ loop-driver) but span four modes that map across the layer-A/layer-B split:
   - **Conversation** (gates, reflections, questions) → **layer A**, loop-driver finishes with text. The discriminator keys on `tools[]` *presence* not intent, so these route to the driver too: finish-with-text is **frequent, not an edge case** — the scenario *"Loop-driver finishes with a text completion when no further action is needed"* is more load-bearing than its placement suggests (the driver must default to **not acting** when a turn does not warrant a tool, or it would `write` when asked a question at a gate).
   - **Generating an artifact/code** (write an ADR, write a module) → **layer B**, callee ensemble generates; terminal emits `write`/`edit`. Accounted for *structurally*; whether an ensemble writes a *good* ADR is ensemble quality — declared orthogonal to Cycle 7 at DISCOVER ("ship delegation reliability; ensemble quality iterates independently").
   - **Reasoning about artifacts** (read an essay, audit an ADR against it, synthesize a trail) → **splits**: reasoning-that-*produces* output is layer B (callee); reasoning-that-*decides the next step* from an observed `read` result is layer A (loop-driver, via grounded carry + WP-LB-C loop participation).
   - **Code work** (TDD: write → `bash` test → diagnose → fix → re-run) → same split: generation is layer B; deciding "fix vs. move on" from observed test output is layer A.

   **No mode needs a mechanism the WP-LB design lacks** — `read`/`write`/`edit`/`bash` flow through the terminal (WP-LB-C), results flow back through loop participation + grounded carry. What the artifact-reasoning + code-recovery modes do is **load the axis-2 risk far more heavily than a conversational view implies**: they are sustained, accumulating, error-prone multi-turn trajectories driven by the cheap seat-filler — exactly OQ #27 axis 2 (sequential composition / error-accumulation, the regime AS-9 never tested). **The hardest north-star path is the cheap driver reasoning across a growing artifact set and recovering from test failures, not the conversational path.** This makes WP-LB-B's `TurnDecision`/FC-51 diagnostics more valuable: a driver that misreads an artifact and picks a bad next step shows as a wrong-*action* turn (driver/split), distinguishable from a wrong-*content* turn (callee). It confirms ADR-033 §6b — axis-2 validation must be a **real RDD session** (only RDD naturally produces the reasoning + code-recovery mix), not a synthetic long task.

4. **The discriminator is forced, not chosen (settled-for-build).** `tools[]`-presence is the only architecturally-clean signal: `tool_choice` is stripped at input (Spike κ D0) and ADR-030-deferred; content-classification-as-surface-switch would conflate surface-mode with capability-routing and violate AS-10 (layer-A/layer-B separation); last-message-is-tool-result misses the first agent turn. So the coarseness is non-negotiable and is *compensated by* the loop-driver's finish-with-text capability (signal #3).

5. **Cross-client validate-not-assume (carried to PLAY/first-deployment).** "Agent turns carry `tools[]`" is observed (Spike π, OpenCode 1.15.5), not specified. When the north star widens past OpenCode (Aider/Cursor/Cline), each client's `tools[]`-shaping is a fresh validation event per advisory #2 — the discriminator does not get less correct, but its grounding is per-client.

6. **Scope boundary the WP-LB set does NOT cover: the richer tool surface (`skill`/`task`/`todowrite`).** The surface RDD-via-OpenCode *literally* drives is `skill` (invoke the RDD skill), `task` (subagents), and `todowrite` (tracking) on top of `read`/`write`/`edit`/`bash`. ADR-033 §6c names the full surface but scopes Cycle 7 BUILD to the **file-action tools** — `skill`/`task`/`todowrite` are "north-star context ARCHITECT/BUILD must not be blindsided by," explicitly deferred. So WP-LB-A..F deliver "ensemble work lands on the client's filesystem" (the loop-back's purpose), **not** "drive a full RDD session." The literal run-RDD-via-OpenCode flow is the file-action subset in Cycle 7; the richer surface is a follow-on. WP-LB-B's loop-driver should map the file-action tools and not silently mishandle an unmapped `skill`/`task`/`todowrite` call (treat as a named validation event, consistent with advisory #2).

7. **Wrapper-residual watch point under artifact-reasoning (ADR-033 F3-1).** If RDD's artifact-reasoning frequently needs *within-a-single-turn* multi-capability composition (read 3 docs AND synthesize, in one step), that is the recorded wrapper residual — the place OQ #26's callee resolution could reopen. Across-turn composition (read, read, synthesize as three turns) is callee-native and fine, and RDD mostly decomposes across turns, so callee holds. This is a PLAY/first-deployment watch point, not a BUILD blocker.

### From Cycle 7 loop-back ARCHITECT (closed at gate 2026-06-02)

1. **Four new modules decompose the tool-driven multi-turn surface.** Loop Driver (L2; layer-A control structure, per-turn callee delegation, swappable seat-filler, axis-2 `TurnDecision` diagnostics), Single-Step Enforcer (L2; batch-truncation grounding guarantee), Artifact Bridge (L2; `read_deliverable` → tool-call content marshalling), Client-Tool-Action Terminal (L3; `tool_calls` emission + multi-turn loop participation). Two extensions (Serving Layer surface-mode discrimination; Session Artifact Store `read_deliverable`). Dispatch Pipeline scoped to single-turn. Full entries + responsibility matrix + 9 cycle-free edges + integration contracts + FC-42..FC-52 + test architecture in `system-design.agents.md`. **BUILD decomposes these as roadmap WP-LB-A..F.**

2. **D2 = batch-truncation; D1 = Serving-Layer discriminator** (both ARCHITECT-resolved, not deferred). Batch-truncation is the only τ′-evidenced enforcement candidate and is model-independent (so the seat-filler stays swappable, FC-46); the two untested candidates (re-planning prompt; one-tool `tool_choice`) remain BUILD-tunable behind the Single-Step Enforcer boundary (`tool_choice` weakest per Spike κ). The surface-mode discriminator (`len(request.tools) > 0`) is a named Serving-Layer function, **validate-not-assume** — treat the first unexpected `tools[]` pattern from a tool-capable client as a named validation event (BUILD advisory 2), not a defect.

3. **Six BUILD carry-forward advisories** (from the architect→build snapshot `housekeeping/audits/susceptibility-snapshot-cycle-7-loopback-architect.md`; No Grounding Reframe), priority order: (1) **confirm the FC-51 scope** with the practitioner before WP-LB-F — the ARCHITECT-gate refinement made FC-51 a fallback-branch selector (callee-incorrect → wrapper reversion; split-incorrect → Design Amendment), ratified implicitly not explicitly; (2) treat the surface-mode discriminator's first unexpected production signal as a named validation event; (3) keep the D2 tuning window visible (re-planning-prompt candidate has no falsifying evidence); (4) the large-deliverable artifact-bridge fidelity test (FC-49) is a first-class BUILD gate, encoding edge cases in the matrix; (5) confirm the wrapper-contingency fallback ordering (frontier driver first, wrapper second) with the practitioner before the PLAY axis-2 run; (6) **Track A-LB.1 (remove the stale `ClientToolCall` docstring, `v1_chat_completions.py:581-583`) is the non-negotiable first `refactor:` commit** before any loop-back feature work.

4. **Wrapper-contingency fallback ordering (advisory #1 / F3-1 closed at ARCHITECT).** If BUILD/PLAY axis-2 validation shows the cheap driver cannot hold the horizon: **(1) frontier-tier driver first** (a Model Profile swap, FC-46 — preserves the lean callee shape); **(2) wrapper reversion second-order** (Loop Driver delegates per-turn generation to `DispatchPipeline.run()`, FC-52 keeps it accessible) — only if a frontier driver also fails. FC-51's split-vs-callee diagnosis gates this: callee-incorrect → wrapper worth trying; split-incorrect → Design Amendment (the two-layer split itself is implicated).

5. **Axis-2 long-horizon driver coherence is the recorded load-bearing risk (ADR-033 §Decision ¶5), carried to BUILD/PLAY under ADR-097 Conditional Acceptance.** No synthetic test reaches it; FC-51 `TurnDecision` instrumentation (WP-LB-F) makes a failure diagnosable. The seat-filler model is the testable lever (cheap-tier default; frontier-tier fallback — a config change, not re-architecture, per FC-46). North-star-shaped axis-2 validation (a real skill-framework / RDD-via-OpenCode session), not a synthetic long task.

6. **Both Cycle 7 surfaces are BUILD scope; Capability List Builder is shared.** The single-turn surface (first-pass WP-A landed `e538264` + `0a7a822`; WP-B/C/D/E pending — Routing Planner, Response Synthesizer, Capability List Builder + Discovery, Response Labeling) and the tool-driven surface (WP-LB-A..F) coexist behind the surface-mode discriminator. The Loop Driver selects per-turn capabilities from the same **Capability List Builder** (single-turn WP-D). `edit`/`bash`/multi-file/streaming-token coverage beyond `write` is BUILD/PLAY scope (LB-3).

7. **BUILD-mode declaration at entry per ADR-091: recommended gated** — the loop-back carries the axis-2 load-bearing risk + the validate-not-assume discriminator + the FC-51-scope confirmation, all of which want practitioner-in-the-loop stewardship. Auto mode appropriate only once the surface-mode shape + Loop Driver structure are in place and remaining WPs reduce to mechanical wiring.

### From Cycle 7 loop-back DECIDE (closed at gate 2026-06-01)

1. **OQ #26 resolved → callee (ADR-033).** The layer-A loop-driver centers the multi-turn tool-driven chat-completions architecture; per-turn generation is delegated to a single capability ensemble (not the plan→dispatch→synthesize pipeline). ADR-034 adds the client-tool-action terminal + artifact-bridge + multi-turn loop participation. ADR-027 scoped (partial-update header) to the single-turn / layer-B surface. Resolved on the DECIDE-entry wrapper-shaped probe (Spike υ, run deliberately to avoid callee-skew: pipeline-per-turn ~3× latency + redundant planner/synth stages) + practitioner fork resolution. **ARCHITECT decomposes the loop-driver + client-tool-action terminal + artifact-bridge into modules.**

2. **Grounded loop = ADR-097 Conditional Acceptance, conditional on framework-enforced single-action-per-turn.** Spike τ (n=4) falsified the *unconstrained* cheap driver (it batches + presupposes unobserved state — axis-1 failure); Spike τ′ (n=3) passed under single-step enforcement. Grounding is a framework property, not a model assumption. **Axis 2 (long-horizon coherence) is the BUILD/PLAY validation target** and the recorded load-bearing risk. Research log: `essays/research-logs/cycle-7-spike-tau-upsilon-decide-entry-probes.md`.

3. **Six ARCHITECT advisories (from the decide→architect susceptibility snapshot `housekeeping/audits/susceptibility-snapshot-cycle-7-loopback-decide.md`; No Grounding Reframe), priority order:** (1) **specify the wrapper-contingency path** (callee-failure → fallback ordering — F3-1 left it unspecified); (2) treat the **surface-mode discriminator** (branch on client `tools[]`) as **validate-not-assumed** (it is drafting-time synthesis, not driver-derived); (3) **select the single-step enforcement technique** before module decomposition (batch-truncation is the τ′-backed prior; re-planning prompt + one-tool `tool_choice` are untested candidates); (4) **`SessionArtifactStore.read_deliverable()`** is the first artifact-bridge API addition; (5) add **axis-2 diagnostic instrumentation** so a split-vs-callee failure is distinguishable in BUILD/PLAY; (6) the **refactor-now docstring removal** (`v1_chat_completions.py:581-583`) before BUILD.

4. **Gate-folded constraints (ADR-033, evaluated against the north star at the gate):** **(a) seat-filler swappability is SETTLED** — the loop-driver model is a swappable Model Profile (ADR-011 pattern), so the cheap-vs-capable bet is a config change in BUILD/PLAY, not a re-architecture (this is the precondition that makes the bet cleanly testable; the model *choice* is open); **(b) axis-2 validation is north-star-shaped** — a real skill-framework / RDD-via-OpenCode session, not a synthetic long task; **(c) full client tool surface** — the loop-driver must handle OpenCode's full declared surface (`skill`/`task`/`todowrite` beyond `read`/`write`/`edit`/`bash`); file-action tools are the BUILD focus, the richer surface is north-star context ARCHITECT must not be blindsided by.

5. **Conformance debt for ARCHITECT/BUILD** (`housekeeping/audits/conformance-scan-cycle-7-loopback-decide.md`; 12 findings): 1 refactor-now (advisory #6 above) + 9 BUILD-work (loop-driver, single-step enforcement, callee per-turn delegation, tool-call terminal, artifact-bridge, multi-turn loop, `ClientToolCall` re-introduction — the `0a7a822` removal mapped to exact file:line touchpoints) + 2 ARCHITECT-deferral (D1 surface-mode branch placement; D2 single-step enforcement technique). Key structural notes: `_extract_request` (`dispatch_pipeline.py:325-335`) drops `role: "tool"` messages (loop-participation gap); the SSE formatter already handles `ClientToolCall` (streaming terminal ready, no formatter changes); `SessionArtifactStore` is write-only (needs `read_deliverable`); the non-server-side-write FC is satisfied by absence.

6. **Working-preference note for future gates (durable; memory `feedback_outcome_based_over_speculation`):** the practitioner holds an outcome-based view of success and pushed back on grounding-frame questions that ask him to speculate on unobserved results. Once a decision is grounded on available evidence, convert remaining open risk into named BUILD/PLAY validation criteria rather than gate-time speculation; reserve belief-mapping for genuinely examinable assumptions; prefer proposing a settled/open split for confirmation over asking the practitioner to generate speculation. Prefers clean single approaches over outcome-muddying hybrids.

**Settled/open split + full commitment-gating: see gate note `.rdd/gates/cycle-7-loopback-decide-architect-gate.md`.**

### From Cycle 7 loop-back MODEL (closed at gate 2026-06-01)

1. **AS-9 scope-fence (no invariant amendment).** Per-turn agentic-loop-driving is held OUTSIDE AS-9's validated single-decision scope until validated. AS-9's claim is unchanged; the §Scope boundary annotation fences out the new role-shape (layer-A loop-driver). The grounded-loop hypothesis is a working inference (Spike σ, n=1). DECIDE must not treat the loop-driver as covered by AS-9's reliability finding.

2. **AS-9 reopening is TWO-AXIS, not pre-narrowed (widened at the MODEL gate).** If the grounded-loop hypothesis fails, AS-9 reopens along two axes the single-decision basis cannot discriminate: **(1) grounding** — driver slips into ungrounded batch planning; **(2) sequential composition** — trajectory drifts/accumulates error across many decisions even with per-turn grounding intact (the regime AS-9 never tested; an axis-2 failure impugns AS-9's "single-decision-shaped" qualifier itself). **DECIDE-entry falsification probe targets axis 1 only** (cheap, short un-batchable chain); **axis 2 needs a long horizon = BUILD-phase target — the short probe cannot settle it.** A clean short-probe result is an axis-1 pass, NOT full validation; codify as Conditional Acceptance (ADR-097) with axis 2 designated BUILD-phase. **`domain-model.md` OQ #27 is the authoritative two-axis version; the product-discovery grounded-loop inversion is single-axis — read OQ #27, not the inversion, when structuring the probe plan** (snapshot Advisory 1).

3. **AS-10 reaffirmed by Spike ρ (no text change).** A real tool-rich OpenCode client routed correctly via the planner; the prior tool-rich-client routing suppression did NOT recur. Recorded as evidence-reinforcement in Amendment Log #15, not an amendment.

4. **Consolidated DECIDE advisory list** (from MODEL snapshot; 5 advisories): (1) read OQ #27 as authoritative two-axis; (2) short probe settles axis 1 only; (3) **wrapper-shaped probe must be a named deliverable** in the evidence plan, not residual (else OQ #26 settles by callee-skew); (4) three active DISCOVER advisories unchanged — OQ #18 (cost-distribution lens grounding: user-voice vs project-developer-voice), OQ #19 (Tier-1-hybrid vs ADR-027-direct build-complexity comparison before locking PRIMARY), OQ #20 (Population A tool-family timeout research before the latency ADR); (5) ARCHITECT naming-collision flag — "artifact-bridge" (F-ρ.1) ≠ ADR-030 "Bridge mechanism" (`tool_choice`-deferred).

5. **Vocabulary disposition.** 6 terms folded; the 3 DECIDE-pending terms (layer-A loop-driver, layer-B generation, grounded loop) are NOT settled domain vocabulary — disposition resolves when DECIDE selects a layer-A seat-filler.

### From Cycle 7 loop-back DISCOVER (closed at gate 2026-06-01)

1. **The wrapper-vs-callee fork is the cycle's load-bearing open architectural question, held open for DECIDE.** ADR-027's plan→dispatch→synthesize pipeline is a **layer-B (per-turn generation)** mechanism; the north-star session is a multi-turn agentic loop requiring a **layer-A loop-driver** (decide the next agentic step per turn) that no ADR-027 component holds. Disposition (a) **wrapper**: keep the pipeline as the per-turn engine, add a loop-driver + `tool_calls` terminal above it (the "amendment / incomplete-not-wrong" reading). Disposition (b) **callee**: the loop-driver is the center and the pipeline is one of the things the loop calls — or, per Spike σ.2, not the per-turn primitive at all. **The "incomplete, not wrong / aligned with ADR-027's philosophy" framing is the wrapper reading and was deliberately NOT inherited as the default** (loop-back snapshot advisory #1; commitment #3). Product-discovery Tension 21 + Skill Orchestration User loop-back refinement carry the fork.

2. **Evidence-availability asymmetry (DECIDE evidence-plan must address this — snapshot Advisories 2 + 3).** Every multi-turn run the loop-back produced (σ.2) is **callee-shaped**; **no wrapper-as-multi-turn-loop was ever spiked** (ρ ran the pipeline + terminal for a single turn only). So "let the effective path win on evidence" skews callee by default, and BUILD's first runs will too. DECIDE's evidence plan for the fork must include **at least one wrapper-shaped probe** (pipeline as per-turn generation subroutine under a loop-driver), structured alongside an OQ #19-style build-complexity comparison, with named discriminating criteria: reliability over long horizons (the grounded-loop probe), build-complexity / rework, latency compounding across turns, operator-mental-model fit. σ.2's evidentiary weight should get its own row in DECIDE's Tension-21 deliberation, not a parenthetical.

3. **Grounded-loop hypothesis: falsification probe queued for DECIDE entry (snapshot Advisory 4).** The hypothesis (a cheap model can drive the loop because each turn is *grounded* by a real observed tool result — structurally unlike note-22's *ungrounded* multi-dispatch) is a **working inference, NOT a spike finding** (σ.1/σ.2: n=1, short task; σ.2 batched all 3 actions into one planning turn so the "loop" was 2 turns, never a real decide-act-observe chain). **Named discriminating failure** (commitment #5): the driver slips from grounded per-turn stepping into *ungrounded batch planning* — emits a multi-step batch whose later steps presuppose earlier steps' outputs it never observed, and a step fails because the presupposed state did not hold. Run the probe at DECIDE entry against a **harder/longer task than σ.2** (3–5 steps where step 3 depends on step 2's observed output); free local (qwen3:14b/Ollama, $0); ADR-097 Conditional Acceptance is the backstop on mixed results. Practitioner prior 2026-05-31: reasonably solid → probe is grounding-not-blocking.

4. **AS-9 scope note for MODEL.** The grounded-loop hypothesis names a *conditional reopening of AS-9's scope* — specifically around **grounded-vs-ungrounded driving** (not the bounded-role pattern generally) if the hypothesis fails. MODEL should carry this as an explicit AS-9 scope annotation in `domain-model.md`, not silently absorb it. The six new vocabulary terms (layer-A loop-driver, layer-B generation, client-tool-action terminal, parity, artifact-bridge, grounded loop) fold into the glossary; **do NOT promote the three DECIDE-pending terms** (layer-A loop-driver, layer-B generation, grounded loop) to settled domain vocabulary — their disposition resolves when DECIDE selects a layer-A seat-filler (snapshot Advisory 1).

5. **Settled premises into MODEL/DECIDE** (commitment-gating, practitioner-confirmed): text-only terminal **rejected** (endpoint must emit `tool_calls` + participate in the multi-turn loop — justification is the client's execution model, not filesystem geography); **parity** is the bar (behavioral, NOT latency); layer A is a real role ADR-027 lacks; the **artifact-bridge** (F-ρ.1) is a designed-in requirement (production ensembles route deliverables server-side per ADR-025; survives co-location); the loop-back spikes validated **mechanisms at n=1**, not the architecture and not sustained long-horizon. **Open premises:** wrapper-vs-callee; layer-A seat-filler (3 candidates); grounded-loop hypothesis; sustained long-horizon (BUILD-phase validation target).

6. **DECIDE artifact impact preview.** ADR-027 is the most exposed (Tension 21 questions its single-turn shape — amend it or write a companion ADR for the layer-A driver + client-tool-action terminal + multi-turn loop participation). ADR-025 (artifact-as-substrate) intersects via the artifact-bridge. **AS-10** (capability-matching from request content alone) is untouched and **reaffirmed** by Spike ρ (the prior tool-rich-client routing suppression did NOT recur — the planner routes on request content, indifferent to the client's declared tools). New scenarios + interaction-specs needed for the terminal, the bridge, the multi-turn loop, and the parity bar.

### From Cycle 7 BUILD — Track A.3 Spike ν (2026-05-23)

1. **No capability ceiling found.** The long-horizon capability-ceiling question from the architect→build gate is answered for the three under-exercised surfaces: multi-step composition 8/8 (100%) end-to-end with structural-bounding at every step; production-scale numerical ~100% semantic fidelity over 108 figures; adversarial routing judgment defensible on all conformant decisions. The practitioner's belief-mapping concern (hybrid would be preferred if ensembles cannot handle generalized long-horizon tasks) is not triggered by this evidence. Spike ν research log: `essays/research-logs/cycle-7-spike-nu-long-horizon-ceiling.md`.

2. **Single-surface Intermediate (Surface 3, 92.5% conformance); multiple-intermediate ceiling rule did NOT fire.** The Intermediate is planner robustness, not capability: A6 empty-response (reliability), E1/E3 prompt-injection. The trigger condition resolved to "WP-A proceeds with deployment-policy constraint," applied 2026-05-23.

3. **ADR-027 plan-validation is the load-bearing injection defense (carries to WP-A + all downstream).** Spike ν empirically grounded the value of validating the plan (action ∈ {dispatch,direct}; ensemble ∈ registered set) before dispatch — E1's `launch` and E3's `oracle` are rejected → direct. WP-A's two new candidate scenarios encode this as non-optional pipeline behavior. Connects to the ARCHITECT informational observation #7 (AS-10 erosion risk) and ADR-017 (tool-call structural validation guard) — plan validation is the routing-surface analog.

4. **Open robustness/security carry-forwards (not blocking WP-A).** (a) Planner-layer prompt-injection hardening (the framework backstop covers dispatch safety; planner-prompt hardening is the residual) — candidate for a follow-on spike or PLAY-phase probe. (b) Cheap-tier empty-response base rate under production traffic (A6 mode) — PLAY / first-deployment evidence territory; the empty-plan→direct fallback bounds its impact.

5. **Two scoring-artifact findings worth carrying for methodology.** (a) Number-set string-matching produces false positives on value-preserving unit conversions (N1: 48,217 USD-millions → $48.217 billion, correct) — ADR-029's runtime fidelity check must compare numeric value, not string form. (b) In multi-step chains the synthesizer can recover figures a lossy intermediate step dropped, by reading the ORIGINAL REQUEST section (MS2) — information-preserving, but a fidelity-scope nuance for the synthesizer's strict-DISPATCH-RESULTS framing.

### WP-A progress (2026-05-23)

**Decomposition:** ports + spike-backed adapters (practitioner-chosen at WP-A entry).

**Landed + committed:**
- `feat: framework-driven dispatch pipeline + ensemble-backed roles (Cycle 7 WP-A)` — commit `e538264`. New L2 modules `agentic/dispatch_pipeline.py` (DispatchPipeline.run = plan → validate → dispatch → synthesize; Plan→InternalToolCall pure-function adapter; 4 pipeline-stage events; plan validation as non-optional stage backstopping Spike ν E1/E3/A6) and `agentic/ensemble_backed_roles.py` (EnsembleRoutingPlanner / EnsembleResponseSynthesizer over OrchestraService.invoke). 14 unit tests; FC-2 layer map updated (both L2); full suite 2863 green; `make lint` clean. Covers scenarios 1, 2, 5, 6, the adapter, and event emission at the unit level.
- `docs: cycle 7 Spike nu ...` — commit `65431d1`.

**Handler swap (scenario 4) — DONE.** Commit `0a7a822` (`feat: swap chat-completions handler to DispatchPipeline`). `web/api/v1_chat_completions.py` now builds a per-request `DispatchPipeline` via a new async `get_dispatch_pipeline()` factory and drives it through the existing heartbeat + context-sink lifecycle wrappers (retyped via a `_ChatCompletionsCaller` Protocol). Removed the dead runtime-construction code (`_build_runtime`, `get_orchestrator_llm_loader`, `_default_orchestrator_llm_loader`, `get_conversation_compaction`) and the runtime-only chunk branches (`VisibilityEvent` narration, `ClientToolCall` delegation + `_NonStreamingResult.tool_calls`). The three discovery decisions held (context-sink substrate-reg + dispatch-log kept, turn-boundary injection dropped; single-chunk streaming; capability-list interim source). `_reject_reserved_tool_names` retained as a defensive input guard (preserves the Cycle 1 reserved-name commitment; pipeline no longer routes by `tools`).

- **Capability-source correction:** `read_ensembles()` returns `{name, source, relative_path, agent_count, description}` with **no `topaz_skill`** — the cycle-status's stated "read_ensembles filtered by topaz_skill" did not match. `_build_capability_names()` reads names from `read_ensembles()` and the `topaz_skill` marker per-name via `find_ensemble_by_name(name).topaz_skill` (the same EnsembleConfig surface the tier-router skill reader uses). WP-D's Capability List Builder formalizes this as single-source-of-truth.
- **Test disposition (practitioner-decided 2026-05-23):** the 42 handler tests split into 24 preserved-behavior (response shape, request parsing, SSE framing, session-start-once, identity resolution) + 18 removed-behavior (ReAct round-trips, raw-output escape hatch, autonomy/compose narration, Option C client-tool delegation). Practitioner chose **delete all 18** — those behaviors leave the chat-completions surface under ADR-027; the underlying classes keep ~159 tests of independent unit + integration coverage (`test_orchestrator_runtime.py` 24, `test_orchestrator_tool_dispatch.py` 100, `test_autonomy_policy.py` 7, `test_composition_validator.py` 13, + ~15 tool-dispatch integration). The 24 preserved tests were reworked to drive a stub pipeline; 4 handler-level acceptance tests added (scenarios 1/2/4 via a real `DispatchPipeline` + stub ports through the HTTP boundary + reserved-name guard). Handler test file now 28 tests; full suite **2847 green; mypy strict + ruff + format clean; coverage 92%**.
- **Option C narrowing (accepted consequence):** the pipeline emits only `ContentDelta` + `Completion`, so the orchestrator-LLM's mid-turn client-tool delegation is gone from this surface. The Client Tool Surface Commitment is preserved structurally only as "the synthesizer reads prior-turn `tool_calls` in `messages[]`" (per ADR-027 + Spike ε' C1/C2), not as new delegations.

**Step 5 integration verification — handler↔pipeline boundary verified; live-ensemble end-to-end GATED on WP-B/WP-C.** The acceptance tests exercise a real `DispatchPipeline` (plan→dispatch→synthesize) with stub ports through the real HTTP + session + substrate + sink lifecycle. The handler↔pipeline↔**real-ensemble** end-to-end (real Ollama, slow) cannot complete in WP-A: `get_dispatch_pipeline()` points at the production ensemble names `agentic-routing-planner` / `agentic-response-synthesizer`, which do not exist until WP-B / WP-C. This is consistent with **TS-10** ("Dispatch Pipeline operational after WP-A + WP-B + WP-C"). A factory-construction smoke test of `_build_capability_names` + the real adapter wiring (no Ollama) is available if wanted; otherwise live end-to-end lands with WP-B/WP-C.

### From Cycle 7 MODEL (closed at gate 2026-05-22)

1. **AS-9 codified at MODEL boundary.** "Structurally-bounded LLM roles produce reliable output on single-decision-shaped tasks where the orchestrator-LLM-as-decider failed." Empirical basis: 4 documented confabulation modes + 13 tests at qwen3:8b (Spike ε + Spike ε' + Spike μ). **Scope: structural property (role-shape, not model-shape), independent of mechanism choice.** Both candidate mechanisms (ADR-027 framework-driven dispatch pipeline; Tier 1 hybrid with `tool_choice` interception) satisfy AS-9 — the invariant constrains DECIDE's solution space (any architecture must produce structurally-bounded roles) but does not pre-answer the mechanism-choice question.

2. **Mechanism choice remains DECIDE work.** ADR-027-as-primary commitment is unaffected by AS-9 codification — that commitment remains gated by snapshot Advisory 2's build-complexity comparison (OQ #19). DECIDE produces the explicit Tier 1 hybrid vs. ADR-027-direct sprint-effort comparison before ADR-drafting locks the PRIMARY designation.

3. **Spike μ extends empirical coverage of the structural-bounding finding** across four documented confabulation modes (multi-dispatch fabrication per Cycle 6 PLAY note 22; path hallucination per Cycle 6 PLAY note 23; substrate-path-as-deliverable per Spike λ.4-paid/λ.5-paid; coherent factual errors uncalibrated per Cycle 5 PLAY). The "rapid compounding" susceptibility signature from DISCOVER is materially narrower at MODEL exit: combined audit depth grew from "PLAY note 22 + 9 Spike ε/ε' tests" to "4 modes + 13 tests."

4. **AS-9 propagation tasks for DECIDE/BUILD:** examine ADR-021 (per-capability dispatch contract — actor shift for routing decision under AS-9 + ADR-027 direction); update ADR-022 (Routing surface behavior) to reflect AS-9 + ADR-027 remediation per Tension 14 collapse; ADR-014/ADR-015 unchanged. Code references to "orchestrator" / "orchestrator-LLM" need BUILD-phase clarification — under AS-9 + ADR-027 direction, "the orchestrator" refers to the framework-driven dispatch pipeline (the orchestration substrate); the LLM roles are the routing-planner ensemble and response-synthesizer ensemble.

5. **One new DECIDE-phase design question surfaced from Spike μ.1**: Rule 6 candidate for framework-convention enumeration in direct-completion mode. Spike μ.1 showed the synthesizer enumerates `routes.py`, `api.py`, `endpoints.py` as generic conventions with explicit hedging + uncertainty framing when asked "where is X file" questions. Qualitatively different from the PLAY note 23 failure mode but could mislead careless readers. Synthesizer-rule design question (not structural-bounding failure).

6. **Two new MODEL snapshot advisories carry to DECIDE:**
   - **Advisory A (spike methodology — pre-specify qualitative criteria):** future spike work testing the structural-bounding claim against additional failure modes should document qualitative failure-mode criteria before running tests, not only after a pattern-detector flags a fail. The μ.1 reinterpretation was correct; the procedural gap is that correctness depends on documentation produced after the detector result was known. Spike hygiene, not signal of distorted findings.
   - **Advisory B (options-engagement documentation):** DECIDE should not inherit AS-9 as if option (c) (deferral) was examined and rejected at MODEL. The codification option list was not a straw-man menu, but the agent's Finding μ.4 framing pre-argued for option (a); the practitioner's selection of option (a) is recorded without a documented engagement with the deferral case. **Treat AS-9 as correctly codified given the evidence, while holding the amendment pathway open**: if ADR deliberation surfaces reasons the structural-property claim is narrower (e.g., confabulation modes were fixture-based at n=1 per mode for μ.1/μ.3), the domain model supports amendment.

7. **Three DISCOVER advisories carry forward to DECIDE active and unchanged** (per snapshot evaluation — none closed by MODEL work):
   - **Advisory 1 (OQ #18):** cost-distribution lens validation against Population A voice. DECIDE examines whether Tension 18's strict-dispatch disposition is justified by Population A's trust contract (user-voice) or by project-developer value proposition (project-developer-lens).
   - **Advisory 2 (OQ #19):** build-complexity comparison between Tier 1 hybrid and ADR-027-direct per GT-2(a). DECIDE-entry precondition for ADR-027-as-primary commitment.
   - **Advisory 3 (OQ #20):** Population A tool-family timeout research. DECIDE's latency ADR must include OpenCode/Cursor/Cline/Aider timeout-default research; sub-40s for non-streaming would breach transparent-endpoint promise.

8. **OQ #17 preserved as distinct from AS-9.** "Capability matching works from request content alone with no client-side opt-in" remains pending DECIDE codification. AS-9 names the role-shape property (LLM-role bounding); OQ #17 names the request-shape commitment (no opt-in). The distinction was preserved by MODEL deliberately and noted as a positive signal in the snapshot.

9. **Ten new vocabulary entries settled at MODEL** (Amendment Log entry #12) — all 10 DISCOVER-vintage candidates from cycle-status §Cycle 7 DISCOVER feed-forward signal #9 are now binding terminology for DECIDE: Population A, Population B, transparent OpenAI-compatible endpoint, cost-distribution lens (with project-developer-lens vs. user-lens distinction preserved), routing-planner ensemble, response-synthesizer ensemble, framework-driven dispatch pipeline (PRIMARY direction with scope-of-claim partition), structurally-bounded role, `tool_choice` strip-at-input, orchestrator-designs-ensembles (north-star context).

Collapse is session-confirmed-pending-DECIDE-deliberation per snapshot Finding 4.

### From Cycle 7 DISCOVER (closed at gate 2026-05-22)

1. **ADR-027 framework-driven dispatch pipeline is the cycle's PRIMARY direction.** Tier ordering FLIPPED from RESEARCH-close commitment ("hybrid as starting commitment + ADR-027 as escalation") after Spike κ established cost-equivalence + Spike ε empirically validated ADR-027's structural advantage on the routing-decision and post-dispatch-synthesis surfaces. Per GT-2(a) cost-equivalence rule, ADR-027-direct as primary; hybrid as conditional alternative. **Amendment A3 in essay-outline-006 carries this as DECIDE-entry editing work; argument-audit re-run required before DECIDE proceeds beyond corrected Essay-Outline.**

Settled / plausible-but-untested / open buckets explicitly named in essay-outline-006 Amendment A3 Tier 1 reframe + product-discovery.md Orchestrator LLM Cycle 7 refinement. DECIDE/BUILD should honor the partition rather than collapsing it back to "removed entirely."

3. **Spike ε' (gate-tail validation)** — completed 2026-05-22. Closed gate-named plausible-but-untested bounds for direct-completion path, numerical-density fidelity, and multi-turn continuity. Four findings (Rule 5 framing scope; rounding-drift modes; multi-turn continuity validated; tightened scope partition). **No further pre-DECIDE validation spike is required.**

4. **Three susceptibility-snapshot advisories with concrete DECIDE actions:**
   - **Advisory 1 (cost-distribution lens validation against Population A voice)** — the cost-distribution framing in Tension 18 + Amendment A2 is practitioner-voiced and directionally sound; DECIDE/BUILD should validate against independent Population A voice (e.g., review with a Population A operator or examine Population A clients' documentation about expected ensemble behavior).
   - **Advisory 2 (ADR-027-primary build-complexity comparison)** — Spike κ provided cost-equivalence as a premise; the explicit build-complexity comparison between Tier 1 hybrid and ADR-027-direct is DECIDE-entry work. DECIDE should produce the comparison before ADR-drafting locks the PRIMARY designation.
   - **Advisory 3 (Population A tool-family timeout research)** — DECIDE's latency ADR should include OpenCode/Cursor/Cline timeout-default research; if defaults are sub-40s for non-streaming requests, the pipeline's current floor (36s single-step; 64s chained) breaches the transparent-endpoint promise regardless of tuning intentions.

5. **"Rapid compounding" pattern is the cycle's susceptibility signature.** Per snapshot: not standard sycophancy; rather, three spike findings integrated into a single architectural commitment in a single session via a pre-committed rule (GT-2(a)) rather than through deliberative audit depth comparable to RESEARCH's P1-clean process. MODEL should attend to this — the artifact corpus is empirically stronger than Cycle 6 DISCOVER produced, but the integration pattern is novel and warrants stress-testing during MODEL phase vocabulary work and DECIDE phase ADR drafting.

6. **Four spike-derived findings load-bearing for downstream phases:**
   - **Spike ζ (routing-planner viability at qwen3:8b)** — primary C3 mechanism empirically established; latency p50=10s; tuning axes named.
   - **Spike ε (confabulation dissolution on the structural axis)** — orchestrator-LLM-as-decider failure mode dissolved when role is structurally bounded; cheap-tier model (qwen3:8b) succeeds; one Rule 4 rounding drift mode on simple lookup.
   - **Spike κ (D0 — framework drops `tool_choice` at input)** — Pydantic strips `tool_choice` at `_ChatCompletionsRequest` parsing boundary; no code path in `src/llm_orc/` reads or forwards it. Reframes Spike λ + λ-paid findings (correlation not causation; not a model-portability gap). Per Tension 19, the framework-correction question (implement / explicitly reject / reframe out of scope) is a DECIDE ADR.
   - **Spike ε' (gate-tail bounds closing)** — direct-completion path validated across 4 request shapes; rounding drift characterized as two distinct modes (precise-figure rounding + large-number millions rendering); multi-turn continuity validated when prior turns in input (native `messages[]` handling is ARCHITECT-phase mechanical work). Rule 5 framing scope is a DECIDE design question (system prompt sharpening or relaxation).

Production multi-step requires DECIDE design (single-step planner + framework chain-heuristic vs. multi-step planner vs. planner-loops-with-context). Multi-turn continuity validated by Spike ε' C1/C2 — synthesizer-only architecture works when prior turns are in input; production needs native `messages[]` handling (mechanical ARCHITECT-phase work).

Source-code inspection of the request-construction path should be a standard pre-probe step before paid validation spikes characterize provider-side behavior. Future cycles' validation-spike-as-research-method work should inherit this discipline.

Candidate/operator-voice from spike work: routing-planner ensemble, response-synthesizer ensemble. Candidate/architectural-framing: framework-driven dispatch pipeline, structurally-bounded role. ### From Cycle 7 RESEARCH (closed at gate 2026-05-21)

1. **NL-routing fraction under production tool-rich clients is empirically ~0.** Empirically established across Cycle 6 Spike γ + Cycle 6 PLAY notes 1-25 + Spike λ (qwen3:14b) + Spike λ-paid (paid MiniMax M2.5). ADR-022 amendment effectiveness is bounded to bare-endpoint mode; production tool-rich clients (OpenCode confirmed; Aider/Cursor/Cline inferred) all suppress the amendment. Empirically settled.

2. **OpenAI `tool_choice` mechanism is model-portability-gapped.** The framework implements `tool_choice` correctly (validated under qwen3:14b — Spike λ Cell λ.3 dispatched ensemble + clean NL synthesis). The cross-compatibility-relevant production model (paid MiniMax M2.5 via OpenCode Zen) does NOT honor `tool_choice={"name":"invoke_ensemble"}` under tool-rich conditions (Spike λ-paid Cell λ.3-paid). Three candidate diagnoses (Zen proxy stripping; MiniMax non-conformance; framework tool-list interaction) are unresolved — disambiguation is C2 follow-up.

3. **Tiered architecture is the cycle's DECIDE input.** Hybrid (C3 server-side `tool_choice` interception + C4 framework-driven composition continuation + C5 form-drift enforcement at ensemble-authoring layer + C6 fallback design) as starting commitment, ADR-027 framework-driven dispatch pipeline (orchestrator-LLM removed from dispatch path entirely) as structurally pre-committed escalation triggered by hybrid-effectiveness measurement during BUILD/PLAY. Operational measurement criteria are DECIDE-phase work; the cycle commits to criteria existing.

4. **Orchestrator-LLM is the consistent failure surface across three distinct failure modes.** Composition confabulation (Cycle 6 PLAY note 22 — 8 cache-hit web-searcher dispatches + 0 claim-extractor + fabricated final response); positive control (Spike δ — framework-driven chaining produces faithful citations when orchestrator-LLM is removed); post-dispatch protocol-format failure (Spike λ-paid F-paid-4 — substrate-path file-read attempts in XML or as unreachable client-tool calls). The three modes share the orchestrator-LLM as locus; this is the structural finding motivating the ADR-027 escalation path.

5. **Direct-completion fallback is in tension with the project's value proposition.** Practitioner's RESEARCH-gate stance (2026-05-21): *"llm-orc's stance is that ensembles are used to distribute costs and token to distribute, declarative orchestrations of smaller models. So the orchestrator NEEDs to do that. Otherwise we'd simply use the frontier model."* C6 elevates capability-list discovery to first-order requirement (not documentation work), names structured advisory for Population B, and surfaces operator-observable degradation signaling as a deployment concern.

6. **GROUNDING REFRAME GT-1 (DISCOVER entry):** C6's "first-order requirement" elevation was driven by practitioner stance + one PLAY-constructed stakeholder persona (Skill Orchestration User). Independent product-discovery validation is needed before DECIDE treats the value-misalignment framing as load-bearing. DISCOVER should: (a) treat "capability-list discovery is first-order" as a hypothesis for product-discovery examination, not as inherited commitment; (b) apply Population A / Population B belief-mapping (tool-call-aware OpenAI-family clients vs. developer/script clients); (c) cross-reference Cycle 6 PLAY notes 1/18 (direct-completion quality on string-reverse task) vs. note 7 (code-generator ensemble multi-agent run) for empirical quality contrast.

7. **GROUNDING REFRAME GT-2 (DISCOVER→DECIDE boundary):** C7's "hybrid as starting commitment" ordering is asserted to rest on architectural-continuity cost but the cost differential is not quantified. The Abstract's "structurally pre-committed" language slightly overstates the practitioner's verbatim "if hybrid doesn't work empirically → stronger measures" conditional formulation. At the DISCOVER→DECIDE boundary, produce: (a) explicit build-complexity comparison between Tier 1 hybrid implementation and ADR-027-direct implementation; if costs are within same order of magnitude, ADR-027 as primary recommendation; (b) C2 diagnosis disambiguation BEFORE BUILD (Zen-proxy-specific vs. model-specific vs. framework-interaction) — mechanism design for C3 should be conditional on which diagnosis holds.

8. **Empirical-grounding cluster (four working-inference nodes).** E3.1.1 (server-side `tool_choice` interception preserves client-facing API contract); E4.2.1 (production-client filesystem scope is disjoint from agentic-serving deployment's filesystem); E5.3.3 (framework-driven composition continuation eliminates the orchestrator-narration substitution surface); E6.2.1 (project value-proposition centers on ensemble-distributed orchestration such that direct-completion fallback is a value misalignment). Each needs DECIDE-phase corroboration or explicit residual-uncertainty acceptance before BUILD work proceeds.

9. **Validation-spike-as-research-method precedent extended.** Cycle 6 PLAY ran Spike δ in-loop during PLAY; Cycle 7 RESEARCH extended this to Phase A. Two spikes ran during RESEARCH itself (Spike λ cost-free; Spike λ-paid user-authorized ~$0.05-0.30). The anti-elaboration positioning honored — spikes pruned speculative claims at source rather than allowing them to elaborate downstream into ADRs. Future cycles should treat ADR-087 validation spikes as standard RESEARCH method when reframes or design hypotheses touch the production deployment surface.

10. **Stakeholder model shifts for DISCOVER to surface:**
    - **Tool User / Population A (tool-call-aware client without alternative-surface access)** — receives current direct-completion behavior; under C6 framing this is a degradation surface, not a satisfactory default
    - **Tool User / Population B (developer/script client with alternative-surface access)** — can be redirected to `llm-orc invoke` via structured advisory
    - **Skill Orchestration User (Cycle 6 PLAY stakeholder)** — super-objective "Compose a skill framework against the orchestrator's capability library; expect dispatch when a capability slot fits" was empirically unmet; expectation now mediated by `tool_choice` mechanism + capability-list discovery
    - **Orchestrator LLM (as actor)** — role constrained in Tier 1 (routing potentially intercepted server-side; composition continuation removed); removed from dispatch path entirely in Tier 2 (ADR-027)
    - **Ensemble Author / Operator** — new authoring surfaces: routing-planner ensemble (Tier 1 (i') option (i)); synthesizer ensemble (Tier 2 ADR-027); tool-call-as-output-format authoring (Q2 (b))

### From Cycle 6 PLAY (closed at gate 2026-05-20)

1. **Composition drift is in the orchestrator-LLM.** Empirically confirmed by Spike δ. The chain-handling failure does not survive removing the LLM from the chain step.
2. **ADR-022 amendment is bounded to bare-endpoint mode.** Tool-rich clients suppress the amendment regardless of model tier. Production deployments are all tool-rich.
3. **Must-delegate is a bounded claim.** For capability-matched requests it is a current-state constraint; for non-matched it is a future-state aspiration. The fallback path needs explicit design.
4. **Form-vs-content drift may unify.** Schema-as-enforcement could address both in one mechanism.
5. **WP-C orchestrator-context observation works for single-dispatch lookup, fabricates on multi-dispatch summary.** Reading is reliable; narrating across dispatches degrades. Cycle 7 should account for this if any synthesis-of-results role uses the same observation surface.
6. **dispatch_log.json per-request overwrite breaks the operator-facing review use case.** Fix needed (Thread A or in-cycle).
7. **MiniMax-native XML tool-call leakage under bare-endpoint mode** is a model-output-format artifact when no client tools are declared. Not a defect; a tool-surface gap. Worth knowing for client-integration design.
8. **OpenCode interaction shape is preserved under the framework-driven pipeline candidate.** External API stays OpenAI-compatible; internal architecture is what shifts. Tool User mental model holds.

### From Cycle 6 ARCHITECT (closed at gate 2026-05-15)

(retained for reference; see archive for full detail) — `system-design.md` v4.0 + `roadmap.md` v6.0 capture the architecture as of Cycle 6 close. Cycle 7 ARCHITECT will need to update these substantially.

The three original candidates D1 (Zen strips) / D2 (MiniMax ignores) / D3 (framework tool-list interaction) are all moot — they presumed `tool_choice` reached the provider. **Reframes Spike λ findings:** Cell λ.3's qwen3:14b "honors tool_choice" was correlation not causation (the model emergently chose the same answer `tool_choice` would have forced); Cell λ.3-paid's "MiniMax doesn't honor tool_choice" wasn't a model-portability gap — `tool_choice` never reached MiniMax. **Reframes the Phase A reframe:** the Essay-Outline's claim that "the OpenAI `tool_choice` contract already addresses forced routing" is empirically invalidated — the contract is not implemented. Per GT-2(a)'s "if costs are same order of magnitude, ADR-027 as primary recommendation" rule, cost equivalence is now established (both Tier 1 hybrid and ADR-027-direct require new framework code; the "free baseline" assumption fails). Writeup at `essays/research-logs/cycle-7-spike-kappa-tool-choice-diagnosis.md`. Cost: $0.00 (authorized $0.05 budget unspent — available for future κ-derivative work if needed). Methodological observation: source-code inspection should be a standard pre-probe step before paid validation spikes characterize provider-side behavior (ADR-087 amendment candidate).
